# QBIND Whitepaper Contradictions and Undocumented Behaviors

**Version**: 2.0  
**Date**: 2026-05-18  
**Status**: Active Tracking Document

This document tracks contradictions between the whitepaper (`docs/whitepaper/QBIND_WHITEPAPER.md`) and the actual implementation, as well as behaviors that are implemented but not documented.

---

## Contradictions

### C1. O3–O5 Offense Penalties Not Implemented

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Status** | ✅ **RESOLVED (M9/M11)** |
| **Whitepaper Reference** | Section 8.10, Section 12.2 |
| **Code Location** | `crates/qbind-consensus/src/slashing/mod.rs:2218-2240` (PenaltyEngineConfig defaults), `crates/qbind-consensus/src/slashing/mod.rs:2523-2540` (apply_penalty_if_needed O3-O5 handling) |
| **Evidence** | O3-O5 penalties are now fully implemented and enforced: O3 (Invalid Vote): 300 bps (3%) slash + 3 epoch jail; O4 (Censorship): 200 bps (2%) slash + 2 epoch jail; O5 (Availability): 100 bps (1%) slash + 1 epoch jail. Mode matrix: `EnforceCritical`/`EnforceAll` applies penalties for all O1-O5 offenses. |
| **Tests** | `crates/qbind-node/tests/m11_slashing_penalty_o3_o5_tests.rs` (21 tests) |

### C2. No Minimum Stake Requirement

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Status** | ✅ **RESOLVED (M2.1-M2.4)** |
| **Whitepaper Reference** | Section 8.1, Section 12.2, Section 18 |
| **Code Location** | `crates/qbind-system/src/validator_program.rs:130-132` (registration-time enforcement), `crates/qbind-consensus/src/validator_set.rs:116-178` (epoch-boundary filtering via `build_validator_set_with_stake_filter()`), `crates/qbind-node/src/hotstuff_node_sim.rs:936-987` (`with_stake_filtering_epoch_state_provider()`) |
| **Evidence** | Minimum stake is now enforced at both registration and epoch boundary. `min_validator_stake` enforced via `ExecutionContext.min_validator_stake` at registration. `StakeFilteringEpochStateProvider` excludes validators with `stake < min_validator_stake` at epoch transitions. Fail-closed: if all validators excluded, epoch transition fails. |
| **Tests** | `crates/qbind-consensus/tests/validator_set_tests.rs`, `crates/qbind-consensus/tests/m2_2_stake_filter_epoch_transition_tests.rs`, `crates/qbind-node/tests/m2_3_stake_filtering_node_integration_tests.rs`, `crates/qbind-node/tests/m2_4_production_stake_filtering_tests.rs` |

### C4. Production `qbind-node` Binary Does Not Boot a Fully Operating Node

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Status** | ⚠️ **OPEN — partial** (B1, B2, B3 (VM-v0 state restore), B5 (restore-aware consensus start), **B6 (multi-validator P2P binary-path interconnect)**, **B7 (binary-path test-grade KEMTLS bring-up + dialer-side peer-validator identity closure)**, **B8 (listener-side test-grade validator-identity closure + bounded initial-dial retry)**, **B9 (leader-side re-emission of `BroadcastProposal` on late peer connect within the same view)**, **B10 (paired leader-vote re-emission on the same B9 trigger + engine-progress recorder wiring + inbound engine-accept metric closure)**, **B12 (mutual-auth `MutualAuthMode::Required` cryptographic peer-identity binding wired end-to-end through the binary path)**, **bounded multi-validator restore catchup above a restored VM-v0 snapshot prefix**, **B13 (bounded post-catchup restore-mode → normal-participation transition)**, and **B14 (smallest honest binary-path view-timeout / view-change primitive — absent-leader recovery isolated by Run 015)** landed; full production fast-sync/consensus-storage restore, signature verification of `TimeoutMsg`/`TimeoutCertificate`, exponential-backoff timeout pacing, and production PQC KEMTLS AEAD/lifecycle completion still outstanding; Run 039 replaced the pqc-static-root transport KEM with ML-KEM-768 but did not replace DummyAead; **DevNet Evidence Run 018 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_018.md`) further narrows the B13 sub-item: the strict-progress-above-baseline exit predicate in `RestoreCatchupModeState::maybe_exit_after_response` is by design correctness-preserving, but in the specific scenario where a snapshot anchor is sourced from the only continuously-alive peer at the exact moment that peer's own `committed_height` equals the snapshot height and that peer is itself parked sub-quorum, restored validators stay in `mode_active=1` indefinitely and therefore never enter normal participation — so even when a `2f+1` numeric alive set is reachable via additional honest `--restore-from-snapshot` returns, B14 timeout certificates do not form because the restored nodes are gated out of B14 emission while in restore-catchup mode. Run 018 confirms this is a narrow, operationally-mitigable boundary (capture the snapshot anchor only after the live cluster has committed at least one block above the captured anchor) rather than a defect in B13 itself, and it does not affect the already-proven Run-016 three-of-four B14 recovery shape.** **Run 071 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_071.md`) narrows the C4 "trust-bundle hot reload" sub-piece further by landing a mutable-capable shared live PQC trust-context handle (`crates/qbind-node/src/pqc_live_trust.rs::LivePqcTrustState`, an `Arc<RwLock<Arc<LivePqcTrustSnapshot>>>`) that is initialized once at startup from the already-validated `LoadedTrustBundle` and routed through `P2pNodeBuilder::with_live_pqc_trust(...)` into the production-honest PQC mutual-auth handshake configs — replacing the previous closure-captured `PqcStaticRootConfig` / `Arc<HashSet<[u8;32]>>` clones on both the listener-side `TrustedClientRoots` resolver and the bidirectional `LeafCertRevocationList`. Run 071 NEVER mutates the handle after startup (the `swap_snapshot` future-capability is covered by a single unit test only), NEVER connects the handle to `pqc_trust_reload::apply_validated_candidate`, and NEVER weakens Run 069's non-mutation validation/staging boundary or Run 070's `validate → swap → evict_sessions → commit_sequence` ordering contract — the Run 070 CLI hook (`--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply-enabled`) continues to surface `ReloadApplyError::UnsupportedRuntimeContext` honestly because no production session-eviction hook exists yet on the honest PQC path. The remaining C4 sub-piece is the session-eviction hook plus a small `LiveTrustApplyContext` adapter that calls `LivePqcTrustState::snapshot`/`swap_snapshot` + the session-eviction hook + `pqc_trust_sequence::commit_sequence` — once that lands, Run 070's apply contract closes against a running binary without redesigning Run 069 / 070.**) |
| **Whitepaper / Doc Reference** | `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_OPERATIONAL_GUIDE.md` §7–§8 (node bring-up, observability), `docs/ops/QBIND_MONITORING_AND_ALERTING_BASELINE.md` §4 (signal classes A/C/D/E/F), `docs/ops/QBIND_BACKUP_AND_RECOVERY_BASELINE.md` §C1–C5 (recoverability, restore proofs), `docs/release/QBIND_MAINNET_READINESS_CHECKLIST.md` (operability and observability gates) |
| **Code Location** | `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` — `run_local_mesh_node` and `run_p2p_node` spawn `binary_consensus_loop::spawn_binary_consensus_loop` (drives `BasicHotStuffEngine` on a tokio interval) and `metrics_http::spawn_metrics_http_server_with_crypto` (gated by `QBIND_METRICS_HTTP_ADDR` via `MetricsHttpConfig::from_env`); `main.rs` also calls `snapshot_restore::apply_snapshot_restore_if_requested` before consensus startup, and (B5) translates the resulting `RestoreOutcome` into a `binary_consensus_loop::RestoreBaseline` that seeds the engine before the first tick. `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` (B1 wiring + B5 `RestoreBaseline` / `with_restore_baseline`). `crates/qbind-node/src/snapshot_restore.rs` (B3 — validates the existing `meta.json + state/` `StateSnapshotter` format via `validate_snapshot_dir`, materializes the RocksDB checkpoint into `<data_dir>/state_vm_v0`, and writes an append-only `RESTORED_FROM_SNAPSHOT.json` audit marker). `crates/qbind-consensus/src/basic_hotstuff_engine.rs` — **B5** `BasicHotStuffEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline(block_id, height)` and `HotStuffStateEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline(block_id, view, height)` seed `committed_height`, insert the snapshot anchor block into the tree at `height = snapshot_height`, and set `current_view = snapshot_height + 1` so post-restore commits advance above the restored height rather than from zero. `crates/qbind-node/src/cli.rs` — `--restore-from-snapshot <PATH>` plumbed into `FastSyncConfig`. `crates/qbind-ledger/src/state_snapshot.rs` (existing snapshot creation + validation; reused, not re-implemented). |

#### Run 088 update

C4 is narrowed from peer-candidate validation-only receive/send to a hidden, disabled-by-default propagation-only behavior for `0x05` frames. `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-propagation-enabled` allows rebroadcast only after the existing Run 078 / Run 076 validation path succeeds.

The Run 088 path excludes the source peer, uses a local seen cache plus bounded rate/target/queue limits, and does not change the wire format. It does not apply candidates, persist sequence, mutate live trust, evict sessions, or claim consensus ratification.

C4 remains OPEN for peer-driven live apply, activation_epoch runtime source, KMS/HSM custody, in-binary/on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore, and per-environment production trust-anchor operation. C5 remains OPEN / narrowed; Run 088 does not claim C5 closure.

#### Run 089 update

Run 089 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_089.md`,
`scripts/devnet/run_089_peer_candidate_propagation_n3.sh`) lands the
release-binary N=3 DevNet propagation evidence that Run 088 had marked
as incomplete. Three release `qbind-node` processes on loopback
(mutual-auth ML-KEM-768 + ChaCha20-Poly1305 + ML-DSA-44, real consensus
signer keystores, signed DevNet bundle) prove on real binaries that
V0 → V1 → V2 propagation succeeds only after V1's existing Run 076 / 078
validation pipeline accepts the frame, that V1 rebroadcasts to V2 only
(source-peer V0 excluded; `V0.received_total == 0` even after a 5 s
settle window), that invalid wrong-chain candidates do not rebroadcast
(`propagation_suppressed_invalid_total >= 1`,
`propagation_sent_total == 0`), and that duplicate candidates do not
rebroadcast a second time. Across all four propagation scenarios,
`pqc_trust_bundle_sequence.json` is byte-identical on every node before
and after each scenario; all `live_reload_apply_*` and
`session_eviction_*` families remain zero; the
`qbind_p2p_pqc_trust_bundle_peer_candidate_applied_total` family is
absent from `/metrics`; no `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback fires; and
Run 040 / Run 033 lines confirm no active `DummySig` / `DummyKem` /
`DummyAead`. Run 089 does not change wire format, does not apply
candidates, does not introduce peer-driven live apply, and does not
claim full C4 or C5 closure — the same C4 sub-pieces enumerated above
remain OPEN.

#### Run 090 update

Run 090 is a docs-only operator-playbook update that folds the Run
087 safety specification, the Run 088 disabled-by-default
propagation-only prototype, and the Run 089 release-binary N=3
DevNet propagation evidence into a single operator surface in
`docs/ops/QBIND_PQC_TRUST_LIFECYCLE_RUNBOOK.md`. §6.G is renamed to
"Peer-candidate validation-only and propagation-only lifecycle (Runs
076–089)" and gains four new subsections — §6.G.9 (propagation-only
behavior with the `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-propagation-enabled`
flag, the five `..._propagation_*` counters, validation-before-
rebroadcast, source-peer exclusion, local seen-cache / bounded
fanout / fixed-window rate limit / bounded send-queue loop
prevention, and the explicit "no apply / no sequence write / no
`LivePqcTrustState` mutation / no session eviction / no consensus
ratification / no trust-bundle synchronization" invariants), §6.G.10
(operator MAY / MUST NOT split), §6.G.11 (per-scenario evidence
checklist that mirrors what the Run 089 harness asserts on release
binaries), §6.G.12 (Run 087 / 088 / 089 mapping), and §6.G.13
(residual open items). §10 sub-piece 2 is extended to name Run 088
and Run 089 and to re-state that peer-driven live apply is not
implemented and propagation today is opt-in, does not synchronize
trust state, does not ratify consensus, and does not substitute for
the §6.F.4 SIGHUP path. §11 is bumped to "Runs 050–090" with rows
for Runs 088 / 089 / 090. §12 gains the propagation flag and a
propagation-counters subsection. No `crates/**/src/**` change was
required because no runtime contradiction was found. Run 090
explicitly does **not** claim full C4 or C5 closure: every C4 sub-
piece (peer-driven live apply, `activation_epoch` runtime source,
KMS / HSM custody, in-binary / on-chain signing-key ratification,
production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore parity, per-
environment production trust-anchor operation, selective per-peer
session retention, admin-API / filesystem-watcher trigger surface,
multi-validator MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke)
remains OPEN, and C5 remains OPEN / NARROWED only by Runs 038 / 039.

#### Run 091 update

Run 091 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_091.md`,
`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_091_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_tests.rs`)
is a **partial-positive** boundary pin for the C4 sub-piece
"`activation_epoch` runtime source". The investigation surveys
every available epoch source in the codebase
(`MetaStore::get_current_epoch()` / persisted `meta:current_epoch`;
`StateSnapshotMeta`; `BasicHotStuffEngine` consensus state; epoch
manager / transition marker; wall-clock) and records why none are
wired into the trust-bundle activation gate today: `main.rs` does
not open RocksDB before the trust-bundle gate runs;
`StateSnapshotMeta` does not carry an `epoch` field; the consensus
engine is not yet initialized at the trust-bundle gate (circular
dependency: the trust bundle is needed before any block can be
committed); fresh-genesis and snapshot-rejoin both return
`MetaStore::get_current_epoch() = Ok(None)` ambiguously. The
chosen design preserves the existing explicit fail-closed
boundary in `pqc_trust_activation::check_bundle_activation`
(bundle-level + per-active-root `activation_epoch` declared under
`current_epoch = None` ⇒
`TrustBundleActivationError::CurrentEpochUnavailable`) on every
environment (DevNet, TestNet, MainNet) and at every production
call site (startup `--p2p-trust-bundle` load, `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check`,
`--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply`, SIGHUP `LiveReloadController`,
peer-candidate `0x05` validation/propagation), and pins the
boundary with 15 new integration tests:
(1) activation_epoch omitted under any context unchanged;
(2) activation_epoch satisfied accepted;
(3) activation_epoch future rejected (bundle scope);
(4) activation_height satisfied + activation_epoch future rejected;
(5) activation_epoch satisfied + activation_height future rejected;
(6) root-level activation_epoch future rejected (`Root(<root_id_hex>)` scope);
(7) root-level activation_epoch satisfied accepted;
(8/9/10) DevNet / TestNet / MainNet activation_epoch under
unavailable AND height-only context: `CurrentEpochUnavailable`
(no silent ignore on any environment);
(11) reload-check (Run 069 surface) with activation_epoch under
unavailable epoch source rejects with `Bundle(Activation(CurrentEpochUnavailable))`
and the sequence-persistence file is unchanged (no create / no
delete / no mtime / no byte change) — i.e. no sequence number is
burned;
(12) reload-check with future activation_epoch under a SUPPLIED
hypothetical epoch source: rejected, sequence-persistence unchanged;
(13) `TrustBundleRevocation` schema field set has no
`activation_epoch` axis (exhaustive destructure — compile-time gate
against future schema drift, pinning the Run 062 intentional
unsupported-per-entry-revocation-epoch boundary);
(14/15) `CurrentEpochUnavailable` Display contains the
fail-closed phrase, `required_epoch=<n>`, `scope=bundle`, and
never contains "dummy" — operator logs grep the fail-closed
marker safely. Run 091 adds **no new metric families** (the
existing `qbind_p2p_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_required` /
`_activation_epoch_current` gauges plus the combined
`_activation_rejected_total` counter remain the canonical
operator surface; a per-axis `_epoch_rejected_total` /
`_epoch_unsupported_total` would duplicate an existing family
without operator-actionable distinction). Run 091 makes **no
source-code change** under `crates/**/src/**`; the runbook
(`docs/ops/QBIND_PQC_TRUST_LIFECYCLE_RUNBOOK.md` §3.10 / §10.1 /
§11) is annotated with Run 091 cross-references and a Run 091
mapping row. Run 091 does **not** introduce a canonical runtime
epoch source, does **not** introduce a per-environment minimum-
margin policy on the epoch axis, does **not** extend
`TrustBundleRevocation` with `activation_epoch`, does **not**
change the wire envelope, does **not** weaken any Run 050–090
invariant, and does **not** claim full C4 or C5 closure. C4
remains OPEN for the same sub-pieces enumerated in the Run 090
update above (`activation_epoch` runtime source narrowed from
"open with unclear closure path" to "open with a documented
fail-closed boundary today and a documented closure path"; peer-
driven live apply / propagation; KMS/HSM custody; in-binary /
on-chain signing-key ratification; production fast-sync /
consensus-storage restore parity; per-environment production
trust-anchor operation; selective per-peer session retention;
admin-API / filesystem-watcher trigger surface; multi-validator
MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke). C5 is unrelated
and unchanged.

#### Run 092 update

Run 092 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_092.md`) is a
**partial-positive** follow-up to Run 091 that attempts to implement
the narrow canonical pre-consensus epoch-source wiring for PQC
trust-bundle activation using the existing persisted `MetaStore`
(`meta:current_epoch`) value, **if it can be done without broad
storage redesign**. The investigation extends Run 091's source survey
with a Run 092 source-level finding: the production `qbind-node`
binary **does not open** `RocksDbConsensusStorage` (or any
`ConsensusStorage`) anywhere under `crates/qbind-node/src/**` —
`grep -rn "RocksDbConsensusStorage::open"` returns only doc-comments
in `storage.rs`; every real call site lives under
`crates/qbind-node/tests/**` and the `hotstuff_node_sim`
`EpochAwareNodeHotstuffHarness` test harness. `main.rs` therefore
never writes `meta:current_epoch` on a production run, and reading
it would always return `Ok(None)`. The "existing persisted MetaStore
epoch" the task asks Run 092 to wire is structurally present in the
trait / schema / atomic-transition / corruption-guardrail
machinery but is **never persisted by the binary today**. Wiring it
into the trust-bundle activation gate therefore requires (a) deciding
and persisting the consensus-storage on-disk location in
`NodeConfig` (the current `data_dir` layout defines only
`state_vm_v0`); (b) opening `RocksDbConsensusStorage` in `main.rs`
**before** the trust-bundle gate runs and threading the existing
schema-version / incomplete-transition-recovery / corruption-
guardrail surface through the pre-consensus path; (c) wiring the
binary-path consensus loop into `apply_epoch_transition_atomic` so
epoch advances are actually persisted on production runs; (d)
extending `StateSnapshotMeta` with an additive `epoch` field for
snapshot-rejoin parity (out of Run 091 scope and still out of Run 092
scope); and (e) disambiguating fresh-genesis (`Ok(None)`) from
"no canonical source" without silently treating fresh-genesis as
`current_epoch = 0` (which would silently satisfy `activation_epoch
= 0` bundles, exactly the silent-satisfy mode the task forbids).
Together these constitute a broad storage redesign that touches
T112 / M16 / Run 022 / 023 / 057 / 065 / 069 / 070 / 073 / 074 /
076–091 simultaneously and is explicitly out of Run 092 scope.
Run 092 therefore **does not ship the wiring**; it pins the Run 091
fail-closed `CurrentEpochUnavailable` boundary unchanged on every
environment (DevNet / TestNet / MainNet) and every production call
site (startup `--p2p-trust-bundle` load, `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check`,
`--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply`, SIGHUP `LiveReloadController`,
peer-candidate `0x05` validation / propagation), preserves the
Run 050–091 strict ordering exactly (signature → environment →
chain_id → window → revocation → Run 065 minimum-margin → Run 057
height-and-epoch gate → Run 062 per-entry revocation gate →
Run 055 sequence persistence → Run 050 root merge → P2P start),
preserves the Run 070 `validate → swap → evict → commit_sequence`
ordering exactly, and confirms by code inspection of `main.rs:296-303`
/ `:540-547` / `:898-905` / `:939-942` / `:1760-1767` / `:2568` /
`:3418` that every production `ActivationContext` construction
continues to set `current_epoch: None`. Run 092 makes **no source-
code change** under `crates/**/src/**` and **no test change** under
`crates/**/tests/**`; the Run 091 integration test binary
(`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_091_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_tests.rs`,
15 / 15 passing) remains the canonical regression coverage for the
boundary, and the `pqc_trust_activation` lib tests (34 / 34 passing)
remain the canonical unit coverage. Run 092 adds **no new metric
families** (the existing
`qbind_p2p_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_required` /
`_activation_epoch_current` gauges plus the combined
`_activation_rejected_total` counter remain the canonical operator
surface). Run 092 changes only four documentation files:
`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_092.md` (new evidence
record), this `docs/whitepaper/contradiction.md` Run 092 update
section, `docs/ops/QBIND_PQC_TRUST_LIFECYCLE_RUNBOOK.md` (§10.1
cross-reference annotated for Run 091 → Run 092; §11 mapping row
for Run 092), and
`docs/protocol/QBIND_PEER_TRUST_BUNDLE_PROPAGATION_SAFETY.md` (§9
open-questions cross-reference updated to also cite Run 092).
Run 092 narrows the C4 sub-piece "`activation_epoch` runtime source"
from Run 091's "open with documented fail-closed boundary today and
a documented closure path" to Run 092's "open with documented fail-
closed boundary, a documented closure path, AND a Run 092 source-
level confirmation that narrow MetaStore wiring is blocked by the
binary-path storage architecture (no `RocksDbConsensusStorage` is
ever opened by `main.rs`; `meta:current_epoch` is never written on
production runs); closure requires a broad cross-cutting storage /
consensus-loop / snapshot-format redesign run". Run 092 does **not**
close full C4: peer-driven live apply / propagation, KMS/HSM
custody, in-binary / on-chain signing-key ratification, production
fast-sync / consensus-storage restore parity, per-environment
production trust-anchor operation, selective per-peer session
retention, admin-API / filesystem-watcher trigger surface, and
multi-validator MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke
remain OPEN. Run 092 does **not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS
production lifecycle is unrelated to the activation-epoch axis
and is unchanged). Recommended immediate next action: land the
cross-cutting "Run 093 — binary `MetaStore` open + consensus-path
epoch persistence + `StateSnapshotMeta` epoch parity" run, scoped
to the nine steps enumerated in
`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_092.md` §"Immediate next
action recommended".

#### Run 093 update

Run 093 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_093.md`) is a
**partial-positive** follow-up to Run 092 that lands the **minimum
production binary-path `ConsensusStorage` lifecycle and durable
epoch persistence groundwork** required before `activation_epoch`
can be safely consumed for PQC trust-bundle activation. Run 093
closes the storage-lifecycle gap identified by Run 092 — the
production `qbind-node` binary now opens
`RocksDbConsensusStorage` at a single canonical, deterministic
on-disk location (`<data_dir>/consensus`, resolved by the new
`NodeConfig::consensus_storage_dir()` helper) on every production
startup path (LocalMesh and P2P) exactly once per process, runs
the T104 `ensure_compatible_schema` check, runs the M16
`verify_epoch_consistency_on_startup` (incomplete-epoch-transition
recovery) check, probes `meta:current_epoch`, and surfaces a
single explicit
`ConsensusStorageState::{NoConsensusStorage,PresentNoCommittedEpoch,CommittedEpoch(u64)}`
distinction whose `committed_epoch()` accessor returns plain
`Option<u64>` and **collapses neither `NoConsensusStorage` nor
`PresentNoCommittedEpoch` to `Some(0)`** (pinned by
`run_093_does_not_expose_consensus_storage_state_to_activation_context`).
Open / schema / recovery / probe failures all fail-closed with
non-zero exit and an operator-readable error pointing at this
document and `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_093.md`; no
temp fallback, no environment-dependent hidden path, no
`--p2p-trusted-root` fallback, no DummySig / DummyKem / DummyAead.
The opened `Arc<RocksDbConsensusStorage>` handle is held in
`main`'s scope for the binary lifetime and is explicitly logged +
dropped on clean shutdown so the RocksDB lock is released
cleanly. The Run 093 open is inserted at exactly one point in
`main.rs` — **after** `VmV0RuntimeState::open_from_config` (T164)
and **before** the `match config.network_mode` dispatch, **after**
every early-exit validation mode (reload-check, reload-apply,
peer-candidate check) so the existing CLI surface contract
(`--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check` works on DevNet without
`--data-dir`) is preserved. The Run 050–091 strict ordering and
the Run 070 `validate → swap → evict → commit_sequence` ordering
are preserved exactly; Run 093 introduces no call from
`production_consensus_storage` into `pqc_trust_activation`; every
production `ActivationContext` construction site continues to set
`current_epoch: None` exactly as Run 091/092 pinned, so the Run
091 fail-closed `CurrentEpochUnavailable` boundary is preserved
unchanged on every environment (DevNet / TestNet / MainNet) and
every production call site. The Run 091 integration test binary
(`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_091_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_tests.rs`,
15 / 15 passing on Run 093's branch), the `pqc_trust_activation`
lib tests (34 / 34 passing), Run 057 (12 / 12), Run 065 (12 / 12),
Run 069 (12 / 12), Run 073 (10 / 10), Run 074 (10 / 10), Run 076
(16 / 16), Run 088 (5 / 5), the full `qbind-node --lib` (1070 /
1070), `qbind-net --lib` (17 / 17), `qbind-crypto --lib` (68 /
68), and the release builds (`qbind-node` binary +
`devnet_pqc_trust_bundle_helper` + `devnet_pqc_root_helper`
examples) all pass with no regressions. Run 093 ships 7 new unit
tests in `crates/qbind-node/src/production_consensus_storage.rs`
and 12 new integration tests in
`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_093_production_consensus_storage_lifecycle_tests.rs`
covering the canonical path, the three startup-state variants
(`NoConsensusStorage` / `PresentNoCommittedEpoch` / `CommittedEpoch(u64)`),
committed-epoch persistence across simulated restart through the
existing `put_current_epoch` / `get_current_epoch` MetaStore APIs,
RocksDB-lock-held second-open fail-closed, unwritable-data-dir
fail-closed, MetaStore-API-only contract (no parallel epoch-write
path introduced), state-tag stability, and the no-conversion-to-
`ActivationContext` invariant. N=1 release-binary smoke evidence
under `docs/devnet/run_093_smoke_n1_first_start.{stderr,stdout}.log`
and `docs/devnet/run_093_smoke_n1_restart.{stderr,stdout}.log`
proves the canonical `<data_dir>/consensus` path is created on
disk, that the binary logs
`[binary] Run 093 consensus storage: state=present-no-committed-epoch path=<data_dir>/consensus`
on both first start and restart, that T104 + M16 checks ran on
both starts, and that the RocksDB column-family layout
(`CURRENT`, `IDENTITY`, `LOCK`, `LOG`, `MANIFEST-000009`, etc.)
persists between starts. End-to-end committed-epoch persistence
on the release binary is **not yet** proven because the
binary-path consensus loop does not yet emit epoch transitions
onto `apply_epoch_transition_atomic`; this is the documented
partial-positive boundary that a later run (Run 094) must close
by wiring binary-path consensus-loop epoch transitions into the
existing M16 / T112 `apply_epoch_transition_atomic` machinery
using the Run 093 storage handle. Run 093 makes **no** change to
`pqc_trust_activation::ActivationContext`, **no** change to
`StateSnapshotMeta` (snapshot epoch parity remains a separate
cross-cutting run), **no** change to the trust-bundle wire
format, **no** new CLI flag, **no** new metric family, and **no**
new dependency. Run 093 narrows the C4 sub-piece "canonical
production `ConsensusStorage` / `current_epoch` wiring" from Run
092's "open with broad-redesign closure path documented" to Run
093's "**production binary opens canonical `RocksDbConsensusStorage`
at `<data_dir>/consensus` with T104 + M16 checks, the three-way
startup-state distinction is surfaced, the existing MetaStore
epoch-write surface is exercised by the new tests, and the
remaining gap is the narrowly-bounded binary-path consensus-loop
epoch-transition wiring**". Run 093 does **not** close full C4:
binary-path consensus-loop epoch-transition wiring,
`activation_epoch` runtime consumption, snapshot epoch parity
(`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`), peer-driven live apply / propagation
beyond Run 087/088, KMS/HSM custody, in-binary / on-chain
signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-
storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor
operation, selective per-peer session retention, admin-API /
filesystem-watcher trigger surface, and multi-validator MainNet
release-binary peer-connection smoke all remain OPEN. Run 093
does **not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle is
unrelated to the consensus-storage axis and is unchanged).
Recommended immediate next action: land **Run 094 — wire the
binary-path consensus loop's epoch transitions onto
`apply_epoch_transition_atomic` using the Run 093 storage
handle**, scoped to the five steps enumerated in
`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_093.md` §"Exact immediate
next action recommended".

#### Run 094 update

Run 094 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_094.md`) is a
**partial-positive** follow-up to Run 093 that lands the
**smallest production-honest binary-path wiring** that makes
the real `qbind-node` binary persist canonical engine epoch
transitions through the Run 093 `ConsensusStorage` handle.
Run 094 threads the `Arc<RocksDbConsensusStorage>` opened by
Run 093 from `main.rs` through both `run_local_mesh_node` and
`run_p2p_node` into `BinaryConsensusLoopConfig` via a new
`with_consensus_storage(Arc<dyn ConsensusStorage>)` builder
(no `Debug` derive change to the public API — a manual `Debug`
impl prints `<ConsensusStorage handle>` for the new field).
The binary consensus loop initialises `last_persisted_epoch =
engine.current_epoch()` (typically `0` on fresh genesis) and,
on every tick path that may have mutated engine state (the
three existing `update_state_metrics` call sites: inbound-
message handler, ticker tick in the inbound-IO branch, ticker
tick in the no-inbound-IO branch), calls a new public helper
`maybe_persist_engine_epoch_transition(engine, storage,
&mut last_persisted_epoch)` that builds
`EpochTransitionBatch::new(target, previous, reconfig_block_id)`
using `engine.committed_block()` as the reconfig anchor and
issues `apply_epoch_transition_atomic(batch)` through the
threaded handle if and only if `engine.current_epoch()` has
advanced above `last_persisted_epoch`. The persistence
trigger is **exclusively** the engine's own canonical
`current_epoch()` counter — Run 094 invents **no** synthetic
epoch, **no** wall-clock epoch, **no** view-derived epoch,
**no** block-height-derived epoch, and **no** fake transition
just to satisfy tests. Persistence failure is surfaced as a
typed `EpochPersistenceFailed` error (Debug + Display +
`std::error::Error`) carrying `previous_epoch`, `target_epoch`,
`reconfig_block_id`, and the `StorageError` source so
operators can correlate against engine logs; the binary-path
loop logs `[binary-consensus] FATAL: <EpochPersistenceFailed>`
and breaks the tick loop on this error (fail-closed exit),
with the loop-exit summary now including
`last_persisted_epoch=<N> epoch_persistence_failed=<bool>` for
audit. There is **no** silent downgrade to memory-only epoch.
Run 094 reuses the existing M16 atomicity / T104 schema /
incomplete-transition-recovery / corruption-guardrail surface
unchanged. The Run 093 lifecycle (open before network/consensus
dispatch, explicit-drop on shutdown, RocksDB lock release) is
preserved exactly; Run 094 introduces **no** second independent
storage open and **no** new MetaStore key. Run 094 ships **no
source change** to `pqc_trust_activation::ActivationContext` —
every production `ActivationContext` continues to be built with
`current_epoch: None` on every code path; Run 091/092
`CurrentEpochUnavailable` trust-bundle fail-closed behaviour is
preserved unchanged on every environment (DevNet, TestNet,
MainNet). Fresh genesis on the binary path remains
`PresentNoCommittedEpoch` (NOT implicit `0`); the M16 epoch-
consistency check on every observed binary start continues to
log `current_epoch=None`. Run 094 ships 7 new integration tests
in `crates/qbind-node/tests/run_094_binary_path_epoch_transition_persistence_tests.rs`
(all 7 / 7 passing) covering: no-engine-advance no-write,
canonical-advance triggers atomic write, only-engine-current-
epoch is the trigger (32 no-advance no-op calls confirm zero
writes), multi-step advance persists each step once,
`apply_epoch_transition_atomic` write-failure surfaces fail-
closed with the canonical epoch pair (a `FailingStorage` stub
confirms `last_persisted` is NOT advanced on error, error
display contains "fail closed"), end-to-end restart through
the Run 093 surface (`open_production_consensus_storage` →
engine advance → persist → drop → re-open → observe
`CommittedEpoch(11)`), and `ConsensusStorageState::committed_epoch()`
three-variant `Option<u64>` shape pin (no coercion of
`PresentNoCommittedEpoch` into `Some(0)`). The Run 091
integration test binary (`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_091_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_tests.rs`,
15 / 15 passing on Run 094's branch), the Run 093 integration
test binary (12 / 12 passing), `epoch_persistence_tests` /
`epoch_startup_validation_tests` (passing), `binary_path_b1_b2_b4_tests`
(4 / 4), `b5_restore_aware_consensus_start_tests` (4 / 4),
`c4_b6_p2p_binary_path_interconnect_tests` (5 / 5), the full
`qbind-node --lib` (**1070 / 1070**), and the release builds
(`qbind-node` binary, no behavioural change to its release
profile) all pass with no regressions. The `m16_epoch_transition_hardening_tests`
pre-existing compilation error on `set_inject_write_failure`
/ `clear_epoch_transition_marker` (gated behind a `test-utils`
feature not enabled in the default test target) is present on
Run 094's parent commit before any Run 094 change and is NOT
introduced by Run 094. Release-binary smoke evidence
(`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_094.md` §"Release-binary
evidence") captures Scenario 1 (fresh start: canonical
`<data_dir>/consensus` directory created, state
`present-no-committed-epoch`, `[binary] Run 094: binary
consensus loop wired to canonical production ConsensusStorage
handle (LocalMesh).` log line) and Scenario 3 no-transition
restart proof (same state on re-open across process restart,
RocksDB LOCK released cleanly between runs by Run 093's
explicit-drop shutdown path). Scenario 2 (release-binary end-
to-end real epoch transition persistence) is **not exercised
by Run 094** — the production binary-path consensus loop does
not itself trigger a canonical engine epoch transition today
(the engine's `current_epoch()` is initialised to `0` and
only advances when a committed reconfig block is observed
under the existing consensus / epoch rules; the binary-path
consensus loop does not yet process reconfig blocks into
engine `transition_to_epoch` calls). That remaining piece is
the separately enumerated open C4 item *"activation_epoch
real runtime source"* and is explicitly **out of scope** for
Run 094 per `task/RUN_094_TASK.txt` §"Strict non-goals". Run
094 must therefore not fabricate a transition for Scenario 2
— the bounded honest proof we land is the source-level
integration test `run_094_committed_epoch_survives_restart_via_run_093_surface`,
which exercises the **same** `apply_epoch_transition_atomic`
machinery the binary will call, through the **same**
`open_production_consensus_storage` lifecycle the binary uses,
against an engine whose `current_epoch()` has actually
advanced under the engine's canonical setter. Run 094 narrows
the C4 sub-piece "binary-path epoch transition persistence"
from Run 093's "storage opened with the binary-path persistence
trigger as the documented partial-positive boundary" to Run
094's "**production binary opens canonical
`RocksDbConsensusStorage`, threads it into the consensus loop,
and persists `engine.current_epoch()` advances via
`apply_epoch_transition_atomic` with fail-closed error
surface; release-binary end-to-end transition-and-restart
proof remains gated on the separate `activation_epoch` runtime-
source / binary-path reconfig-block-processing work**".
Run 094 does **not** close full C4: `activation_epoch` runtime
consumption, snapshot epoch parity (`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`),
peer-driven live apply / propagation, admin-API / filesystem-
watcher triggers, KMS/HSM custody, on-chain signing-key
ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore,
per-environment production trust-anchor operation, selective
per-peer session retention, and multi-validator MainNet
release-binary peer-connection smoke all remain OPEN. Run 094
does **not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle is
unrelated to the consensus-storage axis and is unchanged).
The persisted epoch exists on the binary path **only after a
real canonical engine epoch transition** — never on a fresh
genesis, never via wall-clock / view / height derivation, and
never via a fabricated transition path. Fresh genesis remains
no-epoch, **not** epoch `0`. Trust-bundle activation still
does not consume `current_epoch`. Run 091/092 fail-closed
behaviour remains intact. Recommended immediate next action:
land **Run 095 — wire the binary-path consensus loop's
reconfig-block commit detection onto
`BasicHotStuffEngine::transition_to_epoch` using the existing
reconfig block schema**, scoped to the four steps enumerated
in `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_094.md` §"Exact
immediate next action recommended". Run 095 will not need to
add any new persistence code — the Run 094 call site will
automatically persist the resulting `engine.current_epoch()`
advance via `apply_epoch_transition_atomic`.

#### Run 095 update

Run 095 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_095.md`) is a
**partial-positive** follow-up to Run 094 that lands the missing
binary-path detection layer between
`engine.commit_log()` and
`BasicHotStuffEngine::transition_to_epoch(...)`. Run 095 adds a
small per-loop `BinaryReconfigDetector` in
`crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` that observes every
proposal the binary loop already sees (leader-emitted via the
`ConsensusEngineAction::BroadcastProposal` arm of `do_leader_tick`,
and inbound via the decoded `BlockProposal` site in
`handle_inbound_consensus_msg`) and caches the canonical wire-level
`(BlockHeader::payload_kind, BlockHeader::next_epoch)` tuple keyed
by the canonical binary-path block ID derivation
(`BlockStore::compute_block_id`, which uses
`(proposer_index, height, parent_block_id)` and matches the engine's
internal `derive_block_id_from_header` exactly). On every tick path
that may have advanced `engine.commit_log()`, the loop calls
`maybe_transition_epoch_from_committed_block(&mut engine, &mut
detector)`, which walks newly committed entries, looks up each
entry's cached header, and — for any entry whose cached header is
`PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` — calls the **existing**
`BasicHotStuffEngine::transition_to_epoch(EpochId::new(next_epoch),
engine.validators().clone())` machinery. The same validator set is
threaded across the boundary; Run 095 does **not** redesign
HotStuff commit rules, epoch semantics, or validator-set rotation
(validator-set rotation remains the separately-tracked C4 item
"peer-driven live apply"). The actual committed reconfig block ID
is recorded into the detector and threaded into the Run 094
persistence helper through a new `reconfig_block_id:
Option<[u8; 32]>` parameter, so the persisted `reconfig_block_id`
is the **actual** committed block ID — Run 095 narrows the helper to
return a typed `EpochPersistenceFailureSource::MissingReconfigBlockId`
error when the engine epoch has advanced but no committed reconfig
block ID is supplied, making **zero fallback unreachable on real
transitions**. Malformed or non-monotonic (`next_epoch <=
current_epoch`) reconfig commits are surfaced as
`ReconfigTransitionError::NonMonotonicTargetEpoch`; engine-rejected
transitions (typically `EpochTransitionError::NonSequentialEpoch`)
are surfaced verbatim as `ReconfigTransitionError::EngineRejected`.
In all three failure cases the binary-path loop fails closed — logs
FATAL, records `reconfig_transition_failed=true` or
`epoch_persistence_failed=true` in the loop-exit summary, and breaks
out of the tick loop. Run 095 ships **11 new tests**
(`crates/qbind-node/tests/run_095_binary_path_reconfig_detection_tests.rs`,
11 / 11 passing) covering the detector cache surface, the
non-transition path for normal-kind committed blocks (driven
end-to-end through a real single-validator engine with
`try_propose`), the typed-error display strings, the
`MissingReconfigBlockId` fail-closed write refusal, the
canonical-`reconfig_block_id` happy path, and the engine's own
sequential-monotonicity rule (preserved verbatim by Run 095). All
Run 091/092 activation-isolation tests
(`run_091_pqc_trust_bundle_activation_epoch_tests`), Run 093
production-storage lifecycle tests
(`run_093_production_consensus_storage_lifecycle_tests`, 15 / 15),
Run 094 binary-path persistence tests
(`run_094_binary_path_epoch_transition_persistence_tests`, 7 / 7),
`epoch_persistence_tests`, `epoch_startup_validation_tests`,
`binary_path_b1_b2_b4_tests`, `b5_restore_aware_consensus_start_tests`,
`c4_b6_p2p_binary_path_interconnect_tests`,
`single_node_epoch_transition_tests`,
`t133_mldsa44_epoch_transition_tests`, and the full `qbind-node
--lib` (**1070 / 1070**) all pass with no regressions. The
`m16_epoch_transition_hardening_tests` pre-existing compilation
error on `set_inject_write_failure` / `clear_epoch_transition_marker`
is present on Run 095's parent commit before any Run 095 change
(inherited from the Run 094 parent commit as documented in
`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_094.md`) and is NOT
introduced by Run 095. Release-binary Scenarios 1 (fresh start
remains `present-no-committed-epoch`), 4 (ordinary committed blocks
do not change epoch — covered by the Run 095 unit test
`run_095_normal_committed_blocks_do_not_trigger_transition` driven
end-to-end through a real single-validator engine), and 5
(activation behaviour unchanged — every production
`ActivationContext` still passes `current_epoch: None`) are
preserved verbatim from Run 094 by Run 095. Release-binary Scenario
2 (real committed reconfig transition) and Scenario 3 (restart
proof following Scenario 2) cannot be honestly produced on the
production binary today because the existing binary-path leader
code (`BasicHotStuffEngine::try_propose` in
`crates/qbind-consensus/src/basic_hotstuff_engine.rs:1189..1205`)
hard-codes `payload_kind: PAYLOAD_KIND_NORMAL` and `next_epoch: 0`
into every emitted proposal, and there is no runtime governance or
peer-injection path on the production binary today that would
introduce a canonical `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` proposal into the
binary consensus loop. That residual piece is the separately-
tracked open C4 item "peer-driven live apply" listed in
`task/RUN_095_TASK.txt` §"Current state" and is explicitly **out
of scope** for Run 095 per the task's strict non-goals. Per
`task/RUN_095_TASK.txt` §"Release-binary evidence", Run 095
returns **partial-positive** for that reason and does not fabricate
a binary-path reconfig commit to satisfy Scenario 2. Run 095
narrows the C4 sub-pieces **"binary-path reconfig block
detection"** and **"engine epoch transition trigger"** from Run
094's "binary-path consensus loop does not yet process reconfig
blocks into engine `transition_to_epoch` calls" to Run 095's
"**binary-path consensus loop detects canonical committed
`PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` blocks, validates monotonicity, and calls
`BasicHotStuffEngine::transition_to_epoch(...)` end-to-end; Run 094
persistence then fires with the actual committed
`reconfig_block_id` and no zero fallback; release-binary end-to-end
Scenario 2 remains gated on the separately-tracked peer-driven live
apply work that would introduce a canonical reconfig proposal onto
the binary path**". Run 095 does **not** close full C4:
`activation_epoch` runtime consumption, snapshot epoch parity
(`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`), peer-driven live apply / propagation,
admin-API / filesystem-watcher triggers, KMS/HSM custody, on-chain
signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage
restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation,
selective per-peer session retention, and multi-validator MainNet
release-binary peer-connection smoke all remain OPEN. Run 095 does
**not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle is unrelated
to the consensus-storage / reconfig-detection axis and is
unchanged). Fresh genesis remains no-epoch, **not** epoch `0`.
Trust-bundle activation still does not consume `current_epoch` —
every production `ActivationContext` continues to be constructed
with `current_epoch: None`, including the binary-path activation
site audited by Run 091/092. Run 091/092 `CurrentEpochUnavailable`
fail-closed activation behaviour is preserved verbatim. The
persisted epoch exists on the binary path **only after a real
canonical committed `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` block has been observed
and the engine's existing `transition_to_epoch(...)` machinery has
accepted it** — never on a fresh genesis, never via wall-clock /
view / height derivation, never via a fabricated transition path,
and never with a zero `reconfig_block_id` fallback for a real
transition. Recommended immediate next action: land **peer-driven
live apply / on-chain governance** so the production binary can
honestly produce a committed canonical reconfig block end-to-end
and unlock release-binary Scenario 2 + Scenario 3. The Run 094
persistence call site and the Run 095 detection call site will
then both fire automatically with no further code changes.

| **Description** | The canonical operations docs presume an operable validator binary that, on startup: (a) runs the consensus loop and produces/commits blocks, (b) exposes a Prometheus-compatible `/metrics` endpoint, (c) supports recovery from a state snapshot, and (d) when restoring, resumes consensus from the restored height rather than from zero. **All four are now satisfied at the binary level for the single-validator binary path.** **B13 lands the smallest honest post-catchup restore-mode transition.** Before B13, the binary loop keyed restore-catchup behaviour (periodic `RestoreCatchupRequest` broadcasts and inbound-proposal deferral via `should_defer_restore_proposal_for_catchup`) permanently off `cfg.restore_baseline.is_some()`, an immutable config value. DevNet Evidence Run 012 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_012.md`) documented the resulting boundary: V1B restored from snapshot, caught up to `committed_height=339` / `current_view=342`, but then plateaued — it kept emitting `RestoreCatchupRequest` frames every 10 ticks and would still defer any inbound proposal whose height was more than one above its committed anchor, never transitioning into normal participation. B13 introduces an explicit `RestoreCatchupModeState` local to `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` whose `active` flag starts at `cfg.restore_baseline.is_some()` and flips to `false` exactly once, when (i) an inbound `RestoreCatchupResponse` is processed without rejection, (ii) the running maximum of all observed `responder_committed_height` values has been reached or exceeded by the local engine's `committed_height()`, and (iii) the local committed height is strictly above the snapshot baseline (so we never declare "caught up" without any peer-learned suffix actually committing). The flip is single-shot and fail-closed: malformed/rejected responses do **not** update the peer-anchor tracker, so a hostile or inconsistent payload cannot drive the transition. After the flip, `maybe_broadcast_restore_catchup_request` and `should_defer_restore_proposal_for_catchup` both gate on the dynamic flag instead of the immutable config, so the restored node stops emitting fresh `RestoreCatchupRequest` frames and stops deferring inbound proposals; from that point forward, all forward-progression decisions go through the same `BasicHotStuffEngine::on_proposal_event` / `on_vote_event` paths the non-restore binary path already uses. Two additive `/metrics` gauges expose the transition: `qbind_restore_catchup_mode_active` (0/1) and `qbind_restore_catchup_mode_exited_at_height` (set exactly once at the flip; never decreases). DevNet Evidence Run 013 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_013.md`) now confirms the B13 transition on real binaries in the bounded non-deadlocked case: V1B restored from live-sourced `S=5`, applied 245 peer-learned certified blocks, exited restore-catchup mode at height `246`, flattened catchup requests, and resumed proposal/vote/QC/commit progression to `committed_height=4098`. Seven new unit tests in `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` exercise the transition state machine (no-baseline-no-mode, active-until-caught-up, strict-progress-above-baseline, peer-max running-max, malformed-response stays-active fail-closed, empty-response from caught-up peer, and request-broadcast suppression after exit). All 612 existing `qbind-node` lib tests continue to pass; the single-validator and B5 paths are untouched. **What B13 does NOT solve.** The Run-012 plateau also exhibits a separate, pre-existing limitation of the binary loop: there is no view-timeout / view-change driver, so a view that gets stuck because the leader's proposal was missed by a peer (Run 012's view 342: V0 proposed but V1A died before voting and V1B's startup race meant it never received V0's late-peer-reemit) cannot be advanced by either node's own ticker. Run 013 shows B13's transition fix is **sufficient** for resumed forward progression when the restored node exits catchup into an active proposal/vote path, but it is still not by itself **sufficient** to recover from a fully-deadlocked predecessor view. That deeper boundary (binary-path view-timeout / view-change driver, and/or having the responder piggyback its current pending proposal on a `RestoreCatchupResponse` to a fully-caught-up requester) remains explicitly out of scope and unsolved here. DevNet Evidence Run 014 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_014.md`) materially narrows this further on real binaries: it intentionally recreated the Run-012 deadlocked predecessor-view shape (V0+V1A live to `committed_height=283`/`current_view=286`, V1A then stopped so V0 alone parked at `committed_height=284`/`current_view=287`, 15s deadlock hold, V1B started with `--restore-from-snapshot` from a live-`/metrics`-sourced anchor at `S=43`) and observed that V1B applied 245 peer-learned certified blocks across two real `RestoreCatchupResponse` frames, B13 flipped `RestoreCatchupModeState.active` to `false` exactly at the V0 idle anchor `committed_height=284`, and forward proposal/vote/QC/commit progression then resumed automatically and ran for 280s up to `committed_height=2956`/`current_view=2959`/`view_lag=0`. The unblock was driven by the *already-landed* B9/B10 late-peer-reemit primitive (V0 logged exactly one `B9+B10: re-emitted view 0 BroadcastProposal + BroadcastVote after late peer connect`, loop-exit `outbound_proposal_late_peer_reemits=1`); neither a binary-path view-timeout / view-change driver nor a responder-side pending-proposal piggyback on `RestoreCatchupResponse` was needed for *this* shape. The strictly narrower sliver of the boundary that is still untested by real-binary evidence is therefore the `N≥3` shape where the leader for the next view is the still-absent validator and the late-peer-reemit edge cannot consume the deadlock — a 2-of-2 topology cannot reach that case under leader rotation. Production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore and production PQC KEMTLS root-key distribution remain open as before. B1 + B2 landed earlier; B3 lands the smallest honest restore-from-snapshot startup path: when `--restore-from-snapshot <PATH>` is passed, the binary validates the snapshot via the existing `validate_snapshot_dir` (chain-id, layout, height) and materializes the RocksDB checkpoint into the configured `<data_dir>/state_vm_v0` before consensus starts. **B5 lands the smallest honest restore-aware consensus initialization**: the `RestoreOutcome` produced by B3 is translated into a `RestoreBaseline { snapshot_height, snapshot_block_id }` (using only `StateSnapshotMeta::height` and `StateSnapshotMeta::block_hash` — no invented metadata) and applied via `BasicHotStuffEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline` *before the first tick* of the binary consensus loop. After application, `committed_height = snapshot_height`, the snapshot anchor block is registered in the local block tree at `height = snapshot_height` (so subsequent leader proposals are registered at `snapshot_height + 1`, not `0`), and `current_view = snapshot_height + 1`. The synthetic baseline block carries no `own_qc`, which means the 3-chain commit rule cannot use it as G and therefore cannot fabricate a re-commit at the restored height — only *new* commits above the baseline can fire. Failures (missing path, wrong chain id, missing `meta.json` / `state/`, populated target state dir, missing `--data-dir`) cause a non-zero exit with a precise reason; no silent degradation. **B6 lands the smallest honest multi-validator P2P binary-path interconnect.** Two pre-existing wiring gaps closed: (i) `P2pNodeBuilder` previously plugged a freshly-allocated, immediately-dropped `mpsc::channel::<P2pMessage>` into the inbound demuxer, so every frame the transport actually delivered was silently lost regardless of which `ConsensusInboundHandler` was registered — now the builder calls `p2p_service.subscribe().await` and the demuxer receives the real inbound stream; (ii) the binary consensus loop only consumed leader-step ticks, so even if inbound bytes had reached the loop they would never have entered the engine — a new `BinaryConsensusLoopIo { inbound_rx, outbound }` surface plus a `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` variant now decode `ConsensusNetMsg::Proposal` / `ConsensusNetMsg::Vote` frames into `qbind_wire::consensus::{BlockProposal, Vote}` and feed them into the running `BasicHotStuffEngine` via the existing `on_proposal_event` / `on_vote_event` entry points (the same surfaces that test harnesses already exercise — no new engine API was needed). Engine-emitted `ConsensusEngineAction::{BroadcastProposal, BroadcastVote, SendVoteTo}` flow back out through an existing `ConsensusNetworkFacade` (the real `P2pConsensusNetwork`, which wraps the same `TcpKemTlsP2pService` instance the inbound side reads from — no parallel networking architecture). Sender identity for inbound messages is recovered from `BlockProposal::header.proposer_index` and `Vote::validator_index`, which is the same convention the rest of the codebase already uses (no new peer-identity layer invented). The single-validator / LocalMesh path is preserved bit-equivalent by retaining the existing 4-arg `run_binary_consensus_loop` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop` entry points that delegate to the new `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io(..., None)`. Inbound timeout / new-view frames (`ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout`, `ConsensusNetMsg::NewView`) are explicitly counted as "received but unhandled" rather than silently dropped — the typed `TimeoutMsg` decoder is not yet exposed by `qbind-wire` for general-purpose deserialization, and `NewView` is reserved for future view-change protocol extensions; this is recorded honestly rather than faked as a Noop. B3 + B5 + B6 are scoped to the **single-validator** restore semantics (B3/B5) and to the **honest binary-path inbound→engine routing** (B6); restoring non–VM-v0 substate (e.g. consensus storage at `<data_dir>/consensus`), full production restore sync beyond the bounded peer-certified suffix path, production-grade validator/node-id mapping (today the binary uses the `SimpleValidatorNodeMapping` identity scheme — adequate for the first multi-validator binary-path evidence run, not for production), and the real PQC KEMTLS handshake/identity certificate work all remain out of scope for B6 and are not silently claimed. | **B5 lands the smallest honest restore-aware consensus initialization**: the `RestoreOutcome` produced by B3 is translated into a `RestoreBaseline { snapshot_height, snapshot_block_id }` (using only `StateSnapshotMeta::height` and `StateSnapshotMeta::block_hash` — no invented metadata) and applied via `BasicHotStuffEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline` *before the first tick* of the binary consensus loop. After application, `committed_height = snapshot_height`, the snapshot anchor block is registered in the local block tree at `height = snapshot_height` (so subsequent leader proposals are registered at `snapshot_height + 1`, not `0`), and `current_view = snapshot_height + 1`. The synthetic baseline block carries no `own_qc`, which means the 3-chain commit rule cannot use it as G and therefore cannot fabricate a re-commit at the restored height — only *new* commits above the baseline can fire. Failures (missing path, wrong chain id, missing `meta.json` / `state/`, populated target state dir, missing `--data-dir`) cause a non-zero exit with a precise reason; no silent degradation. **B6 lands the smallest honest multi-validator P2P binary-path interconnect.** Two pre-existing wiring gaps closed: (i) `P2pNodeBuilder` previously plugged a freshly-allocated, immediately-dropped `mpsc::channel::<P2pMessage>` into the inbound demuxer, so every frame the transport actually delivered was silently lost regardless of which `ConsensusInboundHandler` was registered — now the builder calls `p2p_service.subscribe().await` and the demuxer receives the real inbound stream; (ii) the binary consensus loop only consumed leader-step ticks, so even if inbound bytes had reached the loop they would never have entered the engine — a new `BinaryConsensusLoopIo { inbound_rx, outbound }` surface plus a `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` variant now decode `ConsensusNetMsg::Proposal` / `ConsensusNetMsg::Vote` frames into `qbind_wire::consensus::{BlockProposal, Vote}` and feed them into the running `BasicHotStuffEngine` via the existing `on_proposal_event` / `on_vote_event` entry points (the same surfaces that test harnesses already exercise — no new engine API was needed). Engine-emitted `ConsensusEngineAction::{BroadcastProposal, BroadcastVote, SendVoteTo}` flow back out through an existing `ConsensusNetworkFacade` (the real `P2pConsensusNetwork`, which wraps the same `TcpKemTlsP2pService` instance the inbound side reads from — no parallel networking architecture). Sender identity for inbound messages is recovered from `BlockProposal::header.proposer_index` and `Vote::validator_index`, which is the same convention the rest of the codebase already uses (no new peer-identity layer invented). The single-validator / LocalMesh path is preserved bit-equivalent by retaining the existing 4-arg `run_binary_consensus_loop` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop` entry points that delegate to the new `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io(..., None)`. Inbound timeout / new-view frames (`ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout`, `ConsensusNetMsg::NewView`) are explicitly counted as "received but unhandled" rather than silently dropped — the typed `TimeoutMsg` decoder is not yet exposed by `qbind-wire` for general-purpose deserialization, and `NewView` is reserved for future view-change protocol extensions; this is recorded honestly rather than faked as a Noop. B3 + B5 + B6 are scoped to the **single-validator** restore semantics (B3/B5) and to the **honest binary-path inbound→engine routing** (B6); restoring non–VM-v0 substate (e.g. consensus storage at `<data_dir>/consensus`), full production restore sync beyond the bounded peer-certified suffix path, production-grade validator/node-id mapping (today the binary uses the `SimpleValidatorNodeMapping` identity scheme — adequate for the first multi-validator binary-path evidence run, not for production), and the real PQC KEMTLS handshake/identity certificate work all remain out of scope for B6 and are not silently claimed. **B14 lands the smallest honest binary-path view-timeout / view-change primitive needed to recover from the absent-leader N=4 deadlock shape isolated by DevNet Evidence Run 015.** Run 015 had observed the cluster park at `current_view=15` / `committed_height=12` after a restored V1B exited bounded restore-catchup mode (B13 transition fired correctly), because round-robin leader for view 15 in N=4 is `ValidatorId(3)`, who was deliberately absent — and there was no honest mechanism on the binary path to leave that view, so no proposal/vote/QC/commit fired during the 200-second post-restore window. The investigation confirmed this was *not* still-in-restore-mode (catchup requests had already flattened) and *not* a B9/B10 late-peer-reemit gap (no late peer was joining; the leader was simply absent) — it was the missing view-timeout driver itself. The engine surface (`BasicHotStuffEngine::create_timeout_msg`, `mark_timeout_emitted`, `timeout_emitted_in_view`, `on_timeout_msg`, `on_timeout_certificate`) had been present and unit-tested for many milestones, but was entirely unwired on the deployed binary path; correspondingly, inbound `ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout` / `NewView` frames were explicitly counted as "received but unhandled" because no canonical wire decoder existed for `TimeoutMsg`/`TimeoutCertificate`. B14 closes that gap with a strictly minimal change: (1) `serde::{Serialize, Deserialize}` derives are added to `qbind_consensus::QuorumCertificate`, `qbind_consensus::TimeoutMsg`, and `qbind_consensus::TimeoutCertificate` so they have a canonical bincode wire encoding; (2) a new `view_timeout_ticks: Option<u64>` field on `BinaryConsensusLoopConfig` (default `Some(50)` ≈ 5s at the existing 100ms tick interval; `None` disables the primitive entirely and preserves pre-B14 behaviour) controls the threshold; (3) a per-loop `ViewTimeoutState` tracks the most recent tick at which forward view-progress (strict `current_view` advance OR new commit) was observed, resetting the window each time real progress fires so an honest live leader is never timed out; (4) a new `maybe_emit_view_timeout` helper, called once per tick after `do_leader_tick` and after the restore-catchup-mode evaluation, gates emission on five explicit conditions (primitive enabled, restore-catchup mode inactive, outbound facade wired, engine has not already emitted a timeout for this view, window elapsed) and on success builds a `TimeoutMsg` via `engine.create_timeout_msg()`, marks the engine, locally ingests via `engine.on_timeout_msg`, broadcasts the bincode-encoded payload as `ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout(bytes)`, and — if local ingestion already crosses the 2/3 quorum threshold — applies the resulting `TimeoutCertificate` via `engine.on_timeout_certificate` and broadcasts it as `ConsensusNetMsg::NewView(bytes)`; (5) the inbound handlers for `ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout` and `ConsensusNetMsg::NewView` now bincode-decode their payloads and route them through `engine.on_timeout_msg` / `engine.on_timeout_certificate`, with all four failure modes (decode error, validator-set non-membership, insufficient quorum, view mismatch) treated fail-closed via the existing `TimeoutValidationError` surface; (6) ten additive `BinaryConsensusLoopInboundStats` counters (`view_timeouts_emitted`, `inbound_timeouts_delivered`, `inbound_timeouts_engine_accepted`, `timeout_certificates_formed`, `outbound_new_views_sent`, `inbound_new_views_delivered`, `inbound_new_views_engine_accepted`, `view_timeout_advances`, `view_timeout_decode_failures`, `view_timeout_engine_rejects`) expose every step of the primitive on `/metrics`-bound state for the next evidence run. View-timeout emission is **always** suppressed while `RestoreCatchupModeState::active = true` so a restored node never times out a live view it is still catching up to (B13 invariant preserved); single-validator and LocalMesh paths have no outbound facade, so `view_timeouts_emitted` stays at zero on those paths (preserving the B1/B5 single-validator behaviour bit-equivalent). Ten new unit tests in `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` (`b14_view_timeout_emits_after_window_elapses_no_progress`, `b14_view_timeout_suppressed_in_restore_catchup_mode`, `b14_view_timeout_disabled_via_none_emits_nothing`, `b14_view_timeout_progress_resets_window`, `b14_n1_self_quorum_forms_tc_advances_view_and_broadcasts_new_view`, `b14_inbound_malformed_timeout_fails_closed`, `b14_inbound_new_view_with_valid_tc_advances_view`, `b14_inbound_new_view_insufficient_quorum_fails_closed`, `b14_run_015_n4_absent_leader_shape_advances_via_tc`, `b14_single_validator_loop_does_not_emit_timeouts`) exercise the full state machine, including the exact Run-015 N=4 absent-leader shape — local V0 emits its own timeout for view 15, peer V1 and V2 timeouts arrive over the inbound channel, the third one crosses 2f+1 = 3, the engine forms a TC, the loop applies it locally, broadcasts NewView, and `current_view` advances to 16 (whose round-robin leader is V0, not the absent V3); a separate test asserts the single-validator binary path still ends a 60-tick run with `view_timeouts_emitted == 0` because constant QC-driven progress kept the window resetting. All 622 existing `qbind-node` lib tests continue to pass alongside the 10 new ones. **What B14 does NOT solve.** Crypto-signed timeouts (B14 routes `TimeoutMsg` and `TimeoutCertificate` through the engine on the same "no per-message signature verification at the loop level" basis that `Proposal` / `Vote` use today — production hardening of timeout signatures is a separate, additive milestone), exponential-backoff timeout pacing (today the threshold is a fixed tick count; sustained partitions where every view in turn lacks a leader will fire timeouts at the same cadence rather than backing off), per-validator timeout rate limiting on inbound (today only the engine's own duplicate-detection per `(view, validator)` provides bounding), and persistent `TimeoutCertificate` storage across restarts all remain explicitly out of scope. Production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore and production PQC KEMTLS root-key distribution remain open as before. **DevNet Evidence Run 016 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_016.md`) now empirically closes the strict N=4 absent-leader recovery sub-boundary that Run 015 had isolated.** With B14 active by default (`view_timeout_ticks = Some(50)`, ≈ 5 s at 100 ms ticks), the same canonical Run-015 N=4 topology (V0/V1A/V2/V3 live → V1A and V3 SIGINT, V1B restored from a live-`/metrics`-sourced anchor `S=10`) recovered automatically on real `qbind-node` binaries: V1B applied 3 peer-learned certified blocks, B13 exited at `committed_height=11`, B14 then emitted 36 honest `TimeoutMsg` frames per available validator (108 total) — 35 of those per node on `view % 4 == 3` views led by the still-absent V3 (the exact Run-015 plateau shape, recurring under round-robin rotation) — every emit was followed by a successful `TimeoutCertificate` / `NewView` view advance with **zero** decode failures, **zero** engine rejects, and **zero** late-peer-reemit dependencies, and forward proposal/vote/QC/commit progression resumed automatically up to `current_view=155` / `committed_height=116` on V0 / V1B / V2 within ~206 s of post-restore observation (a +105-block advance above the Run-015 plateau). The narrowest things still untested by real-binary evidence are now: multi-absent-leader / sub-quorum-alive shapes where 2 f + 1 timeouts cannot be assembled, large-suffix B13 catchup combined with sustained B14, production-grade signature verification of `TimeoutMsg` / `TimeoutCertificate`, and exponential-backoff timeout pacing. |

#### Run 096 update

Run 096 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_096.md`) is the smallest production-honest binary-path source of canonical reconfig proposals — the residual piece Run 095 explicitly deferred (release-binary Scenario 2 / Scenario 3). Run 096 adds a single-shot, local-operator-gated reconfig proposal intent on `BasicHotStuffEngine` (`pending_reconfig_next_epoch: Option<u64>`, `set_pending_reconfig_next_epoch` / `pending_reconfig_next_epoch` / `clear_pending_reconfig_next_epoch`) and consumes it inside the **existing** `on_leader_step` proposal construction path so that exactly one canonical `BlockHeader { payload_kind: PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG, next_epoch: N, .. }` block is emitted the next time the engine is leader (the previous hard-coded `payload_kind: PAYLOAD_KIND_NORMAL` / `next_epoch: 0` lines in `basic_hotstuff_engine.rs` are replaced by a `take()` of the pending intent under the same `BlockHeader` constructor — no parallel wire format, no second proposal path, no change to block-id derivation or signing). After that single emission the engine clears the intent and returns to normal proposals (single-shot; no spam). The binary loop installs the intent on the engine at startup via a new `BinaryConsensusLoopConfig::with_reconfig_proposal(BinaryReconfigProposalConfig { target_epoch })` builder; the binary CLI surfaces a hidden, disabled-by-default operator flag `--devnet-reconfig-proposal-next-epoch <N>` plumbed through both `run_local_mesh_node` and `run_p2p_node` via the pure helper `derive_reconfig_proposal_from_cli_flag(raw_flag, is_mainnet)` so the environment / validity gates can be unit-tested without spawning a process. The CLI gate refuses `N == 0` (the engine treats 0 as "no epoch requested"; matches `BlockHeader.next_epoch` semantics for `PAYLOAD_KIND_NORMAL`); refuses MainNet (no governance path authorizes operator-gated reconfig proposals on MainNet today — explicitly the Run 095 deferred C4 residual); and refuses non-monotonic targets at the engine layer (`PendingReconfigIntentError::NonMonotonicTarget`). When the canonical reconfig block emitted by the engine commits through the **existing** HotStuff commit rule, the Run 095 detector (`BinaryReconfigDetector::record_observed_proposal` + `maybe_transition_epoch_from_committed_block`) classifies it via the canonical `(payload_kind, next_epoch)` header fields, calls `BasicHotStuffEngine::transition_to_epoch(EpochId::new(N), engine.validators().clone())` end-to-end, and the Run 094 persistence hook (`maybe_persist_engine_epoch_transition`) writes `meta:current_epoch = CommittedEpoch(N)` through the canonical production `ConsensusStorage` handle with the **actual** committed reconfig block ID (Run 095 `MissingReconfigBlockId` fail-closed invariant preserved). Run 096 ships **21 new tests** — 12 engine-side unit tests in `crates/qbind-consensus/src/basic_hotstuff_engine.rs` (intent set/clear/validation, leader proposal carries canonical reconfig fields, one-shot consumption, stale-intent dropped, non-leader does not consume, error-display fail-closed strings) and 9 integration tests in `crates/qbind-node/tests/run_096_binary_path_reconfig_proposal_source_tests.rs` (loop config builder, default-no-intent path is bit-equivalent to pre-Run-096, end-to-end single-validator loop emits `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` → Run 095 detector fires → Run 094 persistence writes `CommittedEpoch(1)`, default-no-intent path leaves storage `PresentNoCommittedEpoch`, CLI gate default-is-none, CLI gate refuses zero / MainNet / accepts valid DevNet). All 21 new tests pass; Run 094 (7 / 7), Run 095 (11 / 11), `binary_path_b1_b2_b4_tests`, `b5_restore_aware_consensus_start_tests`, `b9_late_peer_connect_proposal_reemit_tests`, `b10_engine_acceptance_qc_closure_tests`, `b11_consensus_net_prometheus_coverage_tests`, `qbind-consensus --lib` (162 / 162) and `qbind-node --lib` (1070 / 1070) all pass with no regressions. Run 096 narrows the C4 sub-pieces **"binary-path canonical reconfig proposal source"** and **"release-binary Scenario 2 / Scenario 3 (real committed reconfig transition)"** from Run 095's "binary-path leader code hard-codes `payload_kind: PAYLOAD_KIND_NORMAL` and `next_epoch: 0` into every emitted proposal, and there is no runtime governance / peer-injection path on the production binary today that would introduce a canonical `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` proposal into the binary consensus loop" to Run 096's **"the production `qbind-node` binary now ships a disabled-by-default, hidden, DevNet/TestNet-only, MainNet-refused, operator-gated, single-shot CLI flag that arms exactly one canonical `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` proposal on the next leader-step tick using the existing canonical proposal construction path, with the engine's own monotonicity validation enforced at both intent-arm time and consume time; release-binary Scenario 2 (real committed reconfig transition) and Scenario 3 (restart proof) are now exercised end-to-end by an integration test against the actual `spawn_binary_consensus_loop` entry point"**. Run 096 does **not** close full C4: peer-driven live apply / on-chain governance, peer/gossip propagation of reconfig proposals, admin-API / filesystem-watcher reconfig triggers, MainNet authorization path, validator-set rotation primitive, `activation_epoch` runtime sourcing, snapshot epoch parity (`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`), KMS/HSM custody, in-binary / on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation, selective per-peer session retention, and the N-node MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke all remain OPEN. Run 096 does **not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle is unrelated to the consensus-storage / reconfig-source axis and is unchanged). Fresh genesis still remains no-epoch, **not** epoch `0` (Run 091/092 invariant preserved verbatim; integration test `run_096_default_no_reconfig_intent_does_not_persist_epoch` pins this). Trust-bundle activation still does not consume `current_epoch` — every production `ActivationContext` continues to be constructed with `current_epoch: None`. The persisted epoch exists on the binary path **only after a real canonical committed `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` block has been observed and the engine's existing `transition_to_epoch(...)` machinery has accepted it** — never on a fresh genesis, never via wall-clock / view / height / timer derivation, and never via a fabricated transition path. Run 096's reconfig source is an explicitly **non-governance, DevNet/TestNet-only evidence path**: it produces honest end-to-end Scenario 2 / Scenario 3 evidence under the existing canonical reconfig representation without inventing a parallel wire format or a governance ratification path that does not yet exist.

#### Run 097 update

Run 097 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_097.md`) is a **positive** narrowing of the C4 sub-piece **"snapshot epoch parity"** (the first item on the Run 092 §"Immediate next action recommended" closure list, listed as "snapshot epoch parity (`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`)" on every Run 094 / Run 095 / Run 096 OPEN-list since). Run 097 makes the snapshot/rejoin epoch state honest and durable by extending `StateSnapshotMeta` with an additive `epoch: Option<u64>` field (serialized into `meta.json` only when `Some(n)`; omitted entirely when `None` so pre-Run-097 parsers accept new snapshots byte-for-byte unchanged; malformed / non-integer / negative / quoted epoch values fail closed at `StateSnapshotMeta::from_json`; explicit `"epoch": null` is treated as absence; `Some(0)` is the canonical *committed-epoch-0* signal and is NOT the same as absence — see the seven `run097_*` unit tests in `crates/qbind-ledger/src/state_snapshot.rs`). Run 097 populates the field on snapshot creation from the canonical production `ConsensusStorage::get_current_epoch()` only — the same handle Run 093 opens at `<data_dir>/consensus` and Run 094 persists engine epoch transitions into. The binary-path periodic snapshot helper (`maybe_trigger_periodic_snapshot` in `binary_consensus_loop.rs`) and the SIGUSR1 in-process snapshot trigger (`spawn_vm_v0_snapshot_signal_task` in `main.rs`) now both accept and forward a `Option<&Arc<dyn ConsensusStorage>>` handle, probe `get_current_epoch()`, log the resolved source, and pass the result through a new third argument to `VmV0RuntimeState::create_snapshot(anchor, chain_id, epoch, &metrics)`. The standalone `qbind_state_snapshot` example helper gains a `--epoch <N>` flag (operator MUST source from a canonical surface — Run 097 explicitly forbids deriving epoch from height, view number, wall-clock, timer ticks, snapshot height, filename, or directory name; the snapshot is still produced when no canonical source is available, with `epoch` omitted from `meta.json` rather than fabricated). Run 097 adds a new restore-time function `qbind_node::production_consensus_storage::persist_restored_snapshot_epoch(opened, snapshot_epoch)` that the production `main.rs` calls **after** `apply_snapshot_restore_if_requested` materializes the VM-v0 state (B3) and **after** `open_production_consensus_storage` opens the canonical `<data_dir>/consensus` (Run 093). The function uses the canonical existing `ConsensusStorage::put_current_epoch` API to persist the snapshot's canonical epoch into `meta:current_epoch`, returns `Ok(false)` (no-op) when the snapshot carries `epoch=None` or when the pre-existing CommittedEpoch already matches the snapshot's epoch (idempotent restore), returns `Ok(true)` when a fresh write is performed against a `PresentNoCommittedEpoch` storage, and returns the new `ProductionConsensusStorageError::RestoreEpochInconsistent { existing, snapshot, .. }` (fail-closed) when the pre-existing CommittedEpoch differs from the snapshot's — `main.rs` exits 1 on either `RestoreEpochInconsistent` or `RestoreEpochWriteFailed`, preserving atomicity (a partial restore where VM state is materialized but epoch metadata fails silently is impossible).
