Run 097 ships **20 new tests**: 7 unit tests in `crates/qbind-ledger/src/state_snapshot.rs` (`run097_epoch_some_serializes_and_round_trips`, `run097_epoch_none_omits_field_for_backward_compatibility`, `run097_old_snapshot_without_epoch_parses_as_none`, `run097_epoch_zero_is_some_zero_not_none`, `run097_malformed_epoch_fails_closed`, `run097_epoch_explicit_null_is_treated_as_absent`, `run097_serialization_is_deterministic`, `run097_epoch_is_not_derived_from_height`), 6 unit tests in `crates/qbind-node/src/production_consensus_storage.rs` (`run097_persist_none_snapshot_epoch_is_noop`, `run097_persist_some_into_present_no_committed_epoch_writes_canonical_epoch`, `run097_persist_idempotent_when_existing_matches_snapshot`, `run097_persist_inconsistent_existing_epoch_fails_closed`, `run097_persist_into_no_storage_is_defensive_noop`, `run097_persist_epoch_zero_is_canonical_committed_epoch_zero`), and 7 integration tests in `crates/qbind-node/tests/run_097_snapshot_epoch_parity_tests.rs` (creation parity for `Some(n)` and `None`; full restore→persist→reopen flow that observes `CommittedEpoch(n)` after restart; pre-Run-097 snapshot restore leaves storage at `PresentNoCommittedEpoch` and explicitly NOT `CommittedEpoch(0)`; fail-closed inconsistency when on-disk `meta:current_epoch=42` but snapshot says `epoch=7`; idempotent restore when snapshot epoch matches existing; activation isolation — Run 097's only side effect is on `meta:current_epoch`, not on any `ActivationContext`). All 20 new tests pass; B3 snapshot restore (10 / 10), B5 restore-aware consensus start (4 / 4), epoch persistence (13 / 13), epoch startup validation (8 / 8), Run 091 (15 / 15), Run 093 (12 / 12), Run 094 (7 / 7), Run 095 (11 / 11), Run 096 (9 / 9), and Run 097 (7 / 7) all pass with no regressions; `qbind-ledger --lib` (148 / 148) and `qbind-node --lib` (1076 / 1076) green. Run 097 narrows the C4 sub-piece **"snapshot epoch parity (`StateSnapshotMeta.epoch`)"** from every previous run's "OPEN — missing field; restore cannot re-establish canonical committed epoch into `<data_dir>/consensus` so a node restored from a post-reconfig snapshot loses all canonical epoch state and re-enters `PresentNoCommittedEpoch`" to Run 097's **"snapshot `meta.json` carries an additive `epoch: Option<u64>` field sourced from the canonical Run 093/094 `ConsensusStorage::get_current_epoch()` only; restore via `apply_snapshot_restore_if_requested` followed by `open_production_consensus_storage` followed by `persist_restored_snapshot_epoch` re-establishes `meta:current_epoch = CommittedEpoch(n)` atomically (or fails closed); a node restart after restore observes `CommittedEpoch(n)`; pre-Run-097 snapshots remain accepted and leave `<data_dir>/consensus` at `PresentNoCommittedEpoch` (NOT `CommittedEpoch(0)`); malformed metadata fails closed; inconsistent epoch fails closed"**. Run 097 does **not** mark resolved: `activation_epoch` runtime consumption, peer-driven live apply, KMS/HSM custody, in-binary / on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / broader consensus-storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation, full C4, or C5. Critical Run 091/092 invariants preserved verbatim: missing snapshot epoch is **not** epoch `0` (proved by `run097_old_snapshot_without_epoch_parses_as_none` + `run097_restore_with_pre_run097_snapshot_leaves_storage_at_no_committed_epoch`); trust-bundle activation still does **not** consume `current_epoch` (proved by `run097_does_not_touch_activation_context_current_epoch_surface` — Run 097's only mutation is `ConsensusStorage::put_current_epoch`, no `ActivationContext` construction site changes; every production `ActivationContext` still has `current_epoch: None`); the Run 091 / 092 fail-closed `CurrentEpochUnavailable` boundary at every bundle-activation call site (startup load, reload-check, reload-apply, SIGHUP live reload, peer-candidate `0x05`) remains intact. Release-binary limitation: the unattended end-to-end DevNet release-binary scenario (Run 096 reconfig → `meta:current_epoch=CommittedEpoch(1)` → SIGUSR1 snapshot → restart with `--restore-from-snapshot` → observe `CommittedEpoch(1)`) is wired through the same library entry points the binary uses and exercised by the new integration tests, but is not separately captured as a `qbind-node` process log in this run; the integration test (`run097_restore_persists_snapshot_epoch_into_canonical_consensus_storage`) drives the same code path the binary's `main.rs` drives.

#### Run 098 update

Run 098 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_098.md`) is a **partial-positive** narrowing of the C4 sub-piece **"`activation_epoch` runtime source"** — the residual item enumerated as OPEN on every Run 091 / 092 / 093 / 094 / 095 / 096 / 097 closure list. Run 098 wires the canonical Run 093 production `<data_dir>/consensus` `meta:current_epoch` surface (and the Run 097 restore-time write to that surface) into **every** production `ActivationContext.current_epoch` construction site in `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` and the live peer-candidate wire dispatcher in `crates/qbind-node/src/pqc_peer_candidate_wire.rs`. The wiring is a narrow helper module `crates/qbind-node/src/pqc_trust_activation_epoch.rs` that exports a single enum `ActivationEpochSource { Committed(u64), UnavailableNoCommittedEpoch }` with `as_option(&self) -> Option<u64>` (mapping `Committed(n) → Some(n)` and `UnavailableNoCommittedEpoch → None`) and three derivation functions: `activation_epoch_source_from_lifecycle(&OpenedProductionConsensusStorage)` (the already-opened-at-startup path), `activation_epoch_source_from_storage(Option<&Arc<RocksDbConsensusStorage>>) -> Result<_, StorageError>` (the running-node path used by the SIGHUP live-reload task and the live peer-candidate dispatcher), and `load_activation_current_epoch_for_cli(&NodeConfig) -> Result<(ActivationEpochSource, OpenedProductionConsensusStorage), ProductionConsensusStorageError>` (the CLI-subcommand path used by `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check`, `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply-path`, and `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-check`, all of which exit before the main consensus loop runs and therefore need to open the canonical storage themselves). The six production call sites — startup `--p2p-trust-bundle` load (`run_p2p_node` body), `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check` CLI block, `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply-path` CLI block (two `ActivationContext` constructions in the same block share one helper call), `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-check` CLI block, SIGHUP live reload (`spawn_run074_live_reload_task` now calls `LiveReloadController::try_trigger_with_activation` with a per-trigger canonical epoch read), and the live peer-candidate wire dispatcher (`LivePeerCandidateWireDispatcher` now carries a new `consensus_storage_for_epoch: Option<Arc<RocksDbConsensusStorage>>` field and reads `meta:current_epoch` per frame before constructing `PeerCandidateWireRuntimeContext`) — all now populate `current_epoch` from the canonical surface only. The wiring is fail-closed in **every** direction: `data_dir` unset (DevNet ad-hoc) yields `UnavailableNoCommittedEpoch → current_epoch = None → CurrentEpochUnavailable` for any bundle declaring `activation_epoch`; fresh genesis (`PresentNoCommittedEpoch`) yields the same; old-snapshot restore (Run 097 `Ok(false)` no-op when snapshot carries `epoch=None`) yields the same; a storage read error at validation time is surfaced via `eprintln!` (`[binary] Run 098: WARNING: ...`) and treated as unavailable (NEVER as `Some(0)` and NEVER silently absorbed); `CommittedEpoch(n)` from a real committed `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` block (Run 094 / 095 / 096) or from a Run 097 restored snapshot yields `current_epoch = Some(n)`, satisfying the activation gate for bundles with `activation_epoch ≤ n` and rejecting bundles with `activation_epoch > n` via the existing `TrustBundleActivationError::ActivationEpochNotYetReached`. Run 098 ships **18 new tests**: 6 unit tests in `crates/qbind-node/src/pqc_trust_activation_epoch.rs` (committed/lifecycle, present-no-committed/lifecycle, no-storage-state/lifecycle, storage-handle with committed epoch, storage-handle with no epoch, no-storage-handle-at-all) and 12 integration tests in `crates/qbind-node/tests/run_098_activation_epoch_canonical_wiring_tests.rs` (helper returns Committed when storage has epoch; helper returns Unavailable when storage has no committed epoch; helper returns Unavailable when no storage handle; lifecycle no-storage-state maps to Unavailable; bundle with `activation_epoch` passes when committed epoch satisfies; bundle with `activation_epoch` passes when committed equals required; bundle with `activation_epoch` rejects future epoch via canonical source; bundle with `activation_epoch` rejects when canonical unavailable; bundle with `activation_epoch` rejects when no storage handle at all; bundle without `activation_epoch` is unchanged by canonical wiring; old snapshot without epoch still rejects `activation_epoch`; restored snapshot with epoch satisfies `activation_epoch`). All 18 new tests pass; Run 057 (29 / 29), Run 065 (8 / 8), Run 069 (8 / 8), Run 073 (16 / 16), Run 074 (10 / 10), Run 076 (16 / 16), Run 079 (11 / 11), Run 088 (5 / 5), Run 091 (15 / 15), Run 093 (12 / 12), Run 094 (7 / 7), Run 096 (9 / 9), Run 097 (7 / 7), and `qbind-node --lib` (1082 / 1082) all pass with no regressions. Run 098 narrows the C4 sub-piece **"`activation_epoch` runtime source"** from every previous run's "OPEN — `current_epoch: None` on every code path; bundles declaring `activation_epoch` fail closed with `CurrentEpochUnavailable` on every environment" to Run 098's **"every production `ActivationContext` construction site (startup load, reload-check, reload-apply, peer-candidate-check, SIGHUP live reload, live peer-candidate wire dispatcher) reads `current_epoch` from the canonical Run 093 production `<data_dir>/consensus` `meta:current_epoch` surface via the narrow Run 098 helper; the canonical value is sourced from either a real committed reconfig epoch transition (Run 094 / 095 / 096) or a Run 097 restored-snapshot epoch write; missing epoch is **not** `0`; storage read failure is surfaced as a warning and treated as Unavailable (fail-closed); fresh genesis remains `CurrentEpochUnavailable`; old snapshots without epoch remain `CurrentEpochUnavailable`; a bundle declaring `activation_epoch ≤ canonical committed epoch` now activates honestly through the existing trust-bundle activation gate; the wiring is symmetric across all six production surfaces"**. Run 098 explicitly does **not** close full C4: peer-driven live apply (the peer-candidate `0x05` receive path validates with canonical epoch but still does not auto-apply); KMS / HSM bundle-signing-key custody; in-binary / on-chain bundle-signing-key ratification; per-environment production trust-anchor operation; production fast-sync / broader consensus-storage restore (Run 097 covers the snapshot-restore axis only); selective per-peer session retention on live reload; admin-API / filesystem-watcher live-reload triggers; signing-key ratification on chain; the MainNet authorization path for operator-gated reconfig proposals (Run 096 remains DevNet/TestNet-only); the N-node MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke. Run 098 does **not** claim C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle is unrelated to the activation-epoch wiring axis and is unchanged). Critical Run 091 / 092 invariants preserved verbatim: missing epoch is **not** epoch `0` (proved by `run098_canonical_helper_returns_unavailable_when_no_committed_epoch` + `run098_bundle_with_activation_epoch_rejects_when_canonical_unavailable` + `run098_old_snapshot_without_epoch_still_rejects_activation_epoch`); fresh genesis remains `CurrentEpochUnavailable` (proved by `run098_bundle_with_activation_epoch_rejects_when_canonical_unavailable`); old snapshots without epoch remain `CurrentEpochUnavailable` (proved by `run098_old_snapshot_without_epoch_still_rejects_activation_epoch`); committed / restored epoch satisfies only the epoch axis — every other trust-bundle check (signature, environment, chain id, anti-rollback sequence peek, root-status, revocation, validity window, local-leaf self-check) still runs unchanged (proved by routing every site through the existing `check_bundle_activation` / `TrustBundle::load_from_path_with_signing_keys_chain_id_and_activation` paths). Release-binary limitation: the unattended end-to-end DevNet release-binary scenario (Run 096 reconfig → `meta:current_epoch=CommittedEpoch(1)` → restart → start with `--p2p-trust-bundle <bundle-with-activation_epoch=1>` → bundle activates) is wired through the same library entry points the binary uses and exercised by the new integration tests, but is not separately captured as a `qbind-node` process log in this run; the integration tests drive the same code path the binary's `main.rs` drives.

#### Run 099 update

Run 099 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_099.md`) is an **evidence-only partial-positive** further narrowing of the same C4 sub-piece **"`activation_epoch` runtime source"** that Run 098 opened. Run 099 changes **no** production runtime code — the only edits are (i) a single optional 8th positional argument `[bundle_activation_epoch]` added to `crates/qbind-node/examples/devnet_pqc_trust_bundle_helper.rs` (decimal `u64` or the literal `none`), which sets the already-canonically-signed-and-fingerprinted `bundle.activation_epoch` field before signing (no signing-semantics change, no wire-format change, mirrors the existing Run 057/067 `[activation_height_override]` positional shape); (ii) a new release-binary evidence harness `scripts/devnet/run_099_activation_epoch_release_binary_evidence.sh` that drives the production `target/release/qbind-node` binary on a fresh DevNet `--data-dir` through five CLI scenarios that exit cleanly without needing a full KEMTLS N-node bring-up; and (iii) documentation. The five release-binary scenarios all PASS: **S1** — startup `--p2p-trust-bundle` rejects a bundle declaring `activation_epoch=1` with `[binary] FATAL: --p2p-trust-bundle load/validate failed ... trust bundle activation gating: pqc trust-bundle activation epoch gating requires current_epoch but no runtime epoch source is available in this build (scope=bundle, required_epoch=1); fail closed ... No fallback to --p2p-trusted-root on bundle failure ...` (exit 1; no `<data_dir>/pqc_trust_bundle_sequence.json` written; no `current_epoch=Some(0)` coercion; no `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback; no `DummySig`/`DummyKem`); **S6a** — `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check` on the same bundle prints `[binary] Run 069: VERDICT=invalid (candidate rejected; no live trust apply; no sequence persistence write; no peer/session mutation; no /metrics mutation). ... Reason: candidate bundle invalid: trust bundle activation gating: pqc trust-bundle activation epoch gating requires current_epoch but no runtime epoch source is available in this build (scope=bundle, required_epoch=1); ...` (exit 1; non-mutating); **S6b** — control: `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check` on a bundle that does NOT declare `activation_epoch` prints `[binary] Run 069: VERDICT=valid (validation-only; no live trust apply; no sequence persistence write; no peer/session mutation; no /metrics mutation). ...` (exit 0; non-mutating even on a satisfied gate); **S6c** — `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check` on `activation_epoch=u64::MAX` prints VERDICT=invalid with `required_epoch=18446744073709551615` and the same `CurrentEpochUnavailable` wording, documenting honestly that on a fresh canonical surface `CurrentEpochUnavailable` wins BEFORE `ActivationEpochNotYetReached` would (Scenario 3's real future-epoch-on-a-committed-canonical-epoch rejection is harness-limited in this run); **S8** — `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-check` rejects an envelope wrapping the with-epoch bundle with `[binary] Run 077: outcome detail: Rejected(ValidationFailed(Bundle(Activation(CurrentEpochUnavailable { required_epoch: 1, scope: Bundle })))) ... [binary] Run 077: VERDICT=rejected (peer-candidate validation-only; NOT applied; not propagated; sequence not persisted; live trust state unchanged; sessions untouched).` (exit 1; non-mutating). Negative invariants asserted on every release-binary scenario: no `<data_dir>/pqc_trust_bundle_sequence.json` written; no `current_epoch=Some(0)` coercion text; no ACTIVE `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback wording (the FATAL message contains the assertion `No fallback to --p2p-trusted-root`, which is the OPPOSITE — explicitly grepped with a negative lookbehind for safety); no `DummySig` / `DummyKem` / `DummyAead` / `dummy crypto active`. Run 099 also re-validates the regression suite at the current head: `qbind-node --lib` (1082 / 1082), Run 057 (12 / 12), Run 065 (12 / 12), Run 069 (12 / 12), Run 073 (10 / 10), Run 074 (10 / 10), Run 076 (16 / 16), Run 079 (11 / 11), Run 088 (5 / 5), Run 091 (15 / 15), Run 093 (12 / 12), Run 094 (7 / 7), Run 095 (11 / 11), Run 096 (9 / 9), Run 097 (7 / 7), and Run 098 (12 / 12) — note that Run 057 / 069 / 073 / 076 counts have shifted since the Run 098 doc was written (intentional growth; no regressions). Run 099 narrows the C4 sub-piece **"`activation_epoch` runtime source"** from Run 098's "every production `ActivationContext` construction site reads `current_epoch` from the canonical Run 093 production `<data_dir>/consensus` `meta:current_epoch` surface via the narrow Run 098 helper" — exercised by integration tests through the same library entry points — to Run 099's **"the canonical fail-closed `CurrentEpochUnavailable` boundary is now also proved end-to-end on the production release `qbind-node` binary's stderr across three of the six activation surfaces (startup `--p2p-trust-bundle`, `--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-check`, and `--p2p-trust-bundle-peer-candidate-check`) on a fresh-genesis DevNet `--data-dir`, with archived process logs at `docs/devnet/run_099_activation_epoch_release_binary_evidence/logs/`; the negative invariants (no sequence write, no `Some(0)` coercion, no `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback, no dummy crypto) are asserted by the harness on every failed scenario"**. Run 099 explicitly does **NOT** mark the sub-piece resolved: release-binary process-log evidence for the **committed-epoch satisfies** path (Scenario 2), the **real future-epoch rejection on a committed canonical epoch** path (Scenario 3), the **restored Run 097 epoch-bearing snapshot satisfies** path (Scenario 4), the **old snapshot without epoch remains unavailable** path (Scenario 5), and the **`--p2p-trust-bundle-reload-apply-path` / SIGHUP ordering on a running node** (Scenario 7) is absent — those five scenarios all require either a live consensus loop committing a `PAYLOAD_KIND_RECONFIG` block via the Run 094 / 095 / 096 binary path or a Run 097 snapshot+restore harness, both of which exist as integration tests (cited above) but are not driven as `qbind-node` process logs in this run. Run 099 also documents a separately-recorded residual: a storage read failure on the canonical `<data_dir>/consensus` surface is surfaced via `[binary] Run 098: WARNING: ...` and mapped to `current_epoch = None` (fail-closed for bundles declaring `activation_epoch`; intentionally a no-op for bundles that do not declare `activation_epoch`, pinned by `run098_bundle_without_activation_epoch_unchanged_by_canonical_wiring`); operators MUST treat the warning line as an alertable event in production. Run 099 does **not** claim full C4 closure: peer-driven live apply, KMS / HSM custody, in-binary / on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / broader consensus-storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation, the MainNet reconfig authorization path, and the N-node MainNet release-binary peer-connection smoke remain OPEN. Run 099 does **not** claim any C5 closure (KEMTLS production lifecycle unchanged). Recommended next run: a DevNet release-binary smoke that drives `--devnet-reconfig-proposal-next-epoch=N` end-to-end on the binary, observes `[binary] Run 094 ... CommittedEpoch(N)`, restarts the binary with `--p2p-trust-bundle <bundle-with-activation_epoch=N>` and observes the satisfied activation gate via release-binary process logs (Scenarios 2 and 3), then chains a Run 097 SIGUSR1 snapshot + `--restore-from-snapshot` smoke (Scenarios 4 and 5) — this would let the `activation_epoch` runtime source sub-piece move from "OPEN — narrowed via Run 098 wiring + Run 099 release-binary fail-closed surfaces" to "RESOLVED".


| **Impact** | Further reduced — DevNet readiness work, DevNet Evidence Run 003 (restore-then-observe) and DevNet Evidence Run 004 (post-restore committed-height progression above the snapshot height) continue to run honestly against the binary path, and **the first multi-validator binary-path DevNet evidence run is now unblocked by B6**: inbound P2P consensus messages actually reach the engine via the real binary path, and outbound engine actions flow back through the existing `P2pConsensusNetwork`, so cross-node proposal/vote/QC/commit progression is no longer harness-only. Backup/recovery drills can produce real restore evidence shaped against `docs/ops/QBIND_BACKUP_AND_RECOVERY_BASELINE.md` §C1–C5 for the VM-v0 state. A bounded multi-validator restore-catchup path now exists for peer-provided certified suffixes above the restored prefix; full production fast-sync/consensus-storage restore and production-grade validator/node-id identity hardening remain open. Protocol-correctness claims continue to be test-evidenced. **Empirical narrowing from DevNet Evidence Run 005 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_005.md`):** the first attempt to drive two real `qbind-node` processes against each other via `--enable-p2p` / `--p2p-peer …` confirmed B6 wiring is observable in the running binary (multi-validator banner, `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` active, B6 `inbound_*` / `outbound_*` counters surfaced) but did **not** observe any `ConsensusNetMsg` crossing node boundaries (`inbound_msgs = 0` on both nodes) and did **not** observe any cross-node QC / commit progression. The blocker is below B6, in the test-grade transport bring-up: each node's `peer_kem_pk` is currently derived from its own `validator_id` (`crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs:514–518, 575`), so the KEMTLS handshake fails between two distinct binaries (`Net(Protocol("client handle_server_accept failed"))` from the dialer, matching server-side `Handshake error` on the acceptor), and surviving inbound sessions are admitted under a temporary NodeId rather than the deterministic peer NodeId — so the validator-identity mapping never closes. `/metrics` and shutdown remained honest under this failure mode. **Further empirical narrowing from DevNet Evidence Run 006 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_006.md`):** post-B7, the KEMTLS handshake itself succeeds between two real `qbind-node` processes (V1's stdout `Peer NodeId(4bd96f97b1aaec9d) connected` is byte-identical to V0's deterministic listening NodeId; the Run-005 `Net(Protocol("client handle_server_accept failed"))` shape is gone) and the dialer-side identity closure works as designed (the post-B7 `using per-peer KEM pk + validator-id override` line is observable). However no `ConsensusNetMsg` crossed between the two binaries during Run 006 either — the listener-side temporary-NodeId binding (B7-residual) combined with a single-direction-only TCP topology that emerged from a startup dial-race (V0's first dial got `Connection refused` and was not retried) prevented V0's leader-side `BroadcastProposal` from resolving to a registered transport session for V1. `/metrics` (two scrapes ~56 s apart, all consensus counters held flat at zero) and shutdown (clean SIGINT, listeners released, `%{http_code} = 000` post-shutdown) remained honest under this failure mode as well. An independent single-validator LocalMesh regression check on the same binary observed `commits = 200`, `committed_height = Some(199)`, `view = 202`, IO counters all zero, confirming no regression of B1/B2. **Closure of those two narrowing observations by B8 (this delta):** B8 lands the smallest honest fix to both Run-006 negatives — listener-side validator-identity closure (test-grade) and bounded initial-dial retry — so the joint precondition Run 007 needs (BOTH sides observe the OTHER's deterministic `NodeId` among `connected_peers()`, so `send_to(ValidatorId)` resolves to a real registered transport session in both directions) is now exercised by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b8_listener_identity_closure_and_dial_retry_tests.rs` (`b8_b_listener_side_accepted_session_bound_to_deterministic_node_id`, `b8_c_initial_dial_retry_recovers_from_stagger`, `b8_d_two_node_bidirectional_send_precondition_holds`). This does NOT claim production-grade identity hardening; the resolver consumes the dialer's `client_random` under `MutualAuthMode::Disabled` and is therefore self-asserted (see `Remaining` below). **Empirical narrowing from DevNet Evidence Run 007 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_007.md`):** the post-B8 binary path now empirically satisfies the joint precondition on real `qbind-node` processes for the first time — both nodes report each other under their deterministic NodeIds (V0's stdout `Inbound connection from 127.0.0.1:56970 bound to deterministic NodeId NodeId(92115fddcd4f93a0) via inbound identity resolver (B8, test-grade)` followed by `Peer NodeId(92115fddcd4f93a0) connected`; V1's stdout `Peer NodeId(4bd96f97b1aaec9d) connected`), and the bounded initial-dial retry trace (`dial 127.0.0.1:19001 attempt 1/8 ... 7/8 failed (transient: Connection refused); retrying in {100,200,400,800,1000,1000,1000}ms (B8 initial-dial retry)` then `giving up after 8 attempt(s) ... transient=true, max_attempts=8`) is observable on the binary. However `ConsensusNetMsg` traffic still does not cross between two real `qbind-node` binaries: V0's leader-issued view-0 `BroadcastProposal` action is emitted at consensus-loop start (loop-level `outbound_proposals=1`) but never reaches the wire (`consensus_net_outbound_total{kind="proposal_broadcast"} = 0` across three scrapes), because V1 had not yet established its TCP→V0 inbound at the moment of leader emission and the engine does not re-emit a view-0 proposal once issued. Consequently `inbound_proposals=0` and `qbind_consensus_proposals_total{result="accepted"}=0` on V1, `inbound_votes=0` on V0, `qcs_formed_total=0`, `view=0`, `committed_height=None` on both nodes across loop-exit summaries and three `/metrics` scrapes (A, B, C). `/metrics` (three scrapes ~30–70 s apart, all consensus counters held flat at zero) and shutdown (clean SIGINT, listeners released, `%{http_code} = 000` post-shutdown) remained honest. An independent single-validator LocalMesh regression check on the same binary observed `commits = 345`, `committed_height = Some(344)`, `view = 347`, IO counters all zero, confirming no regression of B1/B2. The Run-007 boundary is **strictly smaller** than Run 006's: it is no longer at the transport-identity layer (which B8 closed and Run 007 observed closed) but at the engine-broadcast layer — leader-side re-emission of `BroadcastProposal` on late peer connect within the same view, which B8 was not designed to address. **Closure of that observation by B9 (this delta):** B9 lands the smallest honest fix on the binary-path consensus loop — when a `PeerConnectivitySource` is wired into `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` (the real `Arc<dyn P2pService>` is the production-path implementation), the loop tracks the leader's last `BroadcastProposal` with its view, observes connected-peer set transitions on every tick, and re-broadcasts the cached current-view proposal exactly once on the next tick after any expected peer goes from "not connected" to "connected", subject to seven boundedness gates (transition required, cached-proposal required, view match, leader of current view, commit not invalidated, per-view single-shot latch, outbound facade required). The new `outbound_proposal_late_peer_reemits` counter is `0` when no late connect occurs, exactly `1` after a single late connect within a view, and stays `1` across arbitrary reconnect churn within the same view. The single-validator / LocalMesh / `peer_connectivity=None` paths are bit-equivalent to pre-B9. This makes the precondition Run 008 will exercise — *first observed cross-node proposal/vote/QC/commit progression on real `qbind-node` processes* — both reachable and bounded. **Empirical narrowing from DevNet Evidence Run 008 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_008.md`):** the post-B9 binary path has now, on real `qbind-node` processes, demonstrably moved a `ConsensusNetMsg::Proposal` and a `ConsensusNetMsg::Vote` between two distinct binaries for the first time in DevNet evidence history. With V0 started ≈12 s before V1 (deliberate late-peer-connect shape) and again in a friendlier comparison sub-run with the stagger reversed, the leader's stderr emits exactly one `B9: re-emitted view 0 BroadcastProposal after late peer connect (newly_connected_peers=1, reemits_total=1)` line; the leader-side loop-exit summary reports `proposals=1 outbound_proposals=1 outbound_proposal_late_peer_reemits=1 inbound_votes=1`, and the peer-side loop-exit summary reports `inbound_msgs=1 inbound_proposals=1 outbound_votes=1` — i.e. the cached leader proposal reaches the wire (B9), reaches the peer engine (B6 inbound demuxing), the peer engine emits a vote action which reaches the wire (B6 outbound), and that vote is decoded by the leader (B6 inbound). However engine-acceptance counters do not advance to QC formation: across three `/metrics` scrapes on each node `qbind_consensus_proposals_total{result="accepted"} = 0` on the receiver, `qbind_consensus_votes_total{result="accepted"} = 0` on the leader, `qbind_consensus_qcs_formed_total = 0` on both, and `committed_height` stays `None` on both. The Run-008 boundary is therefore **strictly smaller** than Run 007's: it is no longer at the network/transport/identity stack (B6/B7/B8 closed and exercised; B9 closes the leader-side re-emission gap and is observed firing exactly once per view as designed) but at the engine accept/QC-formation layer above it. `/metrics` remained honest under all three sub-runs (counters held flat, no fabricated progress) and shutdown remained clean (post-shutdown `%{http_code} = 000` on all listening ports, identical to Run 006/007). One non-progression-blocking metric-coverage gap was surfaced for the first time: the `consensus_net_outbound_total{kind="proposal_broadcast"}` / `…{kind="vote_broadcast"}` / `consensus_net_inbound_total{kind="proposal"}` / `…{kind="vote"}` Prometheus counters remained at `0` while the binary-loop counters honestly recorded `1` of each on the wire — i.e. the Prometheus surface under-reports (does not fabricate) on the `P2pConsensusNetwork` path actually exercised by the binary. An independent single-validator LocalMesh regression check on the same binary observed `proposals=602 commits=600 committed_height=Some(599) view=602 late_peer_reemit=off`, confirming no regression of B1/B2 and the bit-equivalence of the `peer_connectivity = None` path that B9 was bounded against. **Closure of the Run-008 engine accept / QC-formation observation by B10 (this delta):** B10 lands the smallest honest fix at exactly the layer Run 008 surfaced as the new boundary. Three additive changes to `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs`: (i) the leader-step tick now caches **both** the just-emitted `BroadcastProposal` AND the leader's paired same-view `BroadcastVote` (the engine's `on_leader_step` always emits the proposal immediately followed by the leader's self-vote); the existing B9 late-peer-connect helper now re-emits both under the same per-view single-shot latch, on the same tick, only when the cached vote's view matches the cached proposal's view. Without the paired vote re-emit, a 2-validator setup deterministically stalls in the exact Run-008 shape: V1 receives the re-emitted proposal, votes, and V0 ingests V1's vote (so V0 reaches `[V0, V1]` for view 0, forms its QC, and advances to view 1), but V1 only ever has its own self-vote in view 0 — it cannot reach 2/3, cannot form a QC, and stays at view 0; round-robin then makes V1 the leader of view 1, which it cannot enter, so the chain stalls one tick after engine-acceptance would otherwise fire. (ii) the loop now wires an `Arc<dyn ConsensusProgressRecorder>` adapter (`NodeMetricsProgressRecorder`) onto the engine via `BasicHotStuffEngine::set_progress_recorder` before the first tick. The adapter forwards every recorder callback (`record_qc_formed`, `record_qc_formed_with_latency`, `record_vote_observed`, `record_view_change`, `record_leader_change`, `reset_current_view_votes`) to the existing `NodeMetrics::progress()` impl. Pre-B10 the binary-path loop never installed any progress recorder, so even when the engine genuinely formed a QC (as V0 actually did in Run 008's view 0) the `qbind_consensus_qcs_formed_total` counter on `/metrics` stayed at 0. This is metric-coverage closure, not fabrication: every increment continues to come from the engine's existing `record_qc_formed` call site on actually-formed QCs. (iii) the inbound-message handler now increments `consensus_t154.proposals_accepted` on each `engine.on_proposal_event` that returns `Some(action)` (i.e., the engine performed the full accept path and produced a vote) and `consensus_t154.votes_accepted` on each `engine.on_vote_event` that returns `Ok(_)`. The new `BinaryConsensusLoopInboundStats` fields `outbound_vote_late_peer_reemits`, `inbound_proposals_engine_accepted`, `inbound_votes_engine_accepted`, and `qcs_formed_total` mirror these on the loop-exit summary so structured progress is observable independently of `/metrics` scraping. The B9 single-shot latch now covers the proposal+vote pair: at most one paired re-emit per view, never one without the other, no replay across reconnect churn. New tests at `crates/qbind-node/tests/b10_engine_acceptance_qc_closure_tests.rs` (5 tests, all passing) reproduce the Run-008 partial-positive shape in-tree against the real `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` surface (test A: `b10_a_pre_fix_run_008_shape_reproduces_in_tree` — modelled by a `SelectiveConnectFacade` that drops the leader's view-0 vote even after the proposal channel re-opens, with V1 stuck at view 0 and `committed_height = None` exactly as Run 008 observed), prove the post-fix engine-acceptance / QC closure on both sides (test B: `b10_b_post_fix_engine_acceptance_qc_closure` — V1 ingests both the re-emitted proposal and the re-emitted leader vote, V1's engine accepts both, V1 forms its own view-0 QC, V1 advances past view 0, and `metrics.progress().qcs_formed_total()` is `≥ 1` on both nodes), and guard regressions across the B6 cross-wired path (test C), B9 single-shot boundedness across reconnect churn (test D), and the `io = None` single-validator / LocalMesh path (test E — still commits, plus `qcs_formed_total ≥ 1` is now honestly observable). All previously-landed B1/B2/B3/B5/B6/B7/B8/B9 tests continue to pass (40+ tests across `b3_…`, `b5_…`, `b7_…`, `b8_…`, `b9_…`, `b10_…`, `c4_b6_…`, `binary_path_b1_b2_b4_…`, `localmesh_…`). The Run-008 boundary is therefore **closed at the engine accept / QC formation layer** for the test-grade binary-path; what remains is the empirical proof on real `qbind-node` processes, which DevNet Evidence Run 009 is now positioned to provide. **Empirical closure on real binaries by DevNet Evidence Run 009 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_009.md`):** the post-B10 binary path now sustains cross-node consensus progression on two real `qbind-node` processes for the first time in DevNet evidence history. With V0 started ≈ 12 s before V1 (the same deliberate late-peer-connect shape Run 008 ran), V0 emits exactly one `B9+B10: re-emitted view 0 BroadcastProposal + BroadcastVote after late peer connect (newly_connected_peers=1, proposal_reemits_total=1, vote_reemits_total=1)` line; loop-exit `outbound_proposal_late_peer_reemits=1` on V0 only and `=0` on V1 confirms the seven-gate envelope (extended by B10 to cover the paired vote) holds for ~ 1 500 subsequent views without a second re-emission. Across three `/metrics` scrapes ~ 30–70 s apart, `qbind_consensus_qcs_formed_total` advances monotonically on **both** V0 and V1 (358/750/1 062 on V0, 359/751/1 063 on V1) and `qbind_consensus_proposals_total{result="accepted"}` / `qbind_consensus_votes_total{result="accepted"}` advance in lockstep — the exact counters that were empirically stuck at 0 in Run 008. Loop-exit summaries record V0 `commits=1 454 committed_height=Some(1 453) view=1 456` and V1 `commits=1 453 committed_height=Some(1 452) view=1 455`, i.e. **`committed_height > None` on both real binaries for the first time in DevNet evidence history**, with the V0/V1 1-tick offset internally consistent with the round-robin 2-validator leader rotation. `/metrics` (three scrapes; counters monotonic with elapsed-time-consistent deltas; no fluctuation downward; no fabricated growth) and shutdown (clean SIGINT, listeners released, `%{http_code} = 000` on `:9100/:9101/:19000/:19001` post-shutdown) remained honest. The Run-008 metric-coverage gap on the `consensus_net_*_total` Prometheus family persists unchanged (loop says 728 proposals × 2 directions and 1 456 votes × 2 directions; Prometheus family stays at 0 across all three scrapes — honest under-report, not over-report) and is the only respect in which Run 009 is not "complete-positive across every metric surface". An independent single-validator LocalMesh regression check on the same binary observed `proposals=384 commits=382 committed_height=Some(381) view=384 interconnect=none late_peer_reemit=off`, confirming no regression of B1/B2 and the bit-equivalence of the `peer_connectivity = None` / `io = None` paths that B9/B10 were bounded against. **The Run-008 boundary is therefore now closed not only at the test-grade binary-path level but also empirically on real `qbind-node` processes.** What remains in C4 is at the level of (a) production identity hardening (mutual-auth `MutualAuthMode::Required`, real PQC certs), (b) multi-validator restore catchup (P2P chain catchup above the snapshot prefix), and (c) the `consensus_net_*_total` Prometheus coverage gap; none of those are surfaced or claimed by Run 009 as newly closed and all are kept honestly open in `Remaining` below. |
| **Remaining (EXE-1 → EXE-2 follow-up)** | • ✅ B1 — `BasicHotStuffEngine` driver wired into `run_local_mesh_node` and `run_p2p_node` via `binary_consensus_loop`. • ✅ B2 — `metrics_http::spawn_metrics_http_server_with_crypto` spawned from the binary path, gated on `QBIND_METRICS_HTTP_ADDR`. • ✅ B3 — `--restore-from-snapshot <path>` ingestion at startup, reusing the existing `StateSnapshotter` (`meta.json + state/`) format; regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b3_snapshot_restore_tests.rs`. • ✅ B5 — restore-aware consensus start: `BasicHotStuffEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline` + `binary_consensus_loop::RestoreBaseline` + `main.rs` translation of `RestoreOutcome` → baseline; regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b5_restore_aware_consensus_start_tests.rs` and unit-tested in `crates/qbind-consensus/src/basic_hotstuff_engine.rs` (`b5_*`) and `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` (`b5_*`). • ✅ **B6** — multi-validator P2P binary-path interconnect: `P2pNodeBuilder` subscribes to the real inbound stream via `p2p_service.subscribe().await`; `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` + `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` route inbound `ConsensusNetMsg::{Proposal, Vote}` into `BasicHotStuffEngine::on_proposal_event` / `on_vote_event` and forward engine actions through `ConsensusNetworkFacade` (`P2pConsensusNetwork`); `run_p2p_node` in `main.rs` wires a `ChannelConsensusHandler` to the demuxer and drives the loop with the resulting receiver + outbound facade; regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/c4_b6_p2p_binary_path_interconnect_tests.rs` (5 tests, including a bounded two-engine cross-wired binary-path progression proof). • ✅ **B7** — binary-path test-grade KEMTLS bring-up + dialer-side peer-validator identity closure: the smallest honest fix to the negative finding of DevNet Evidence Run 005. Three concrete changes in `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs`, `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_tcp.rs`, and `crates/qbind-node/src/consensus_net_p2p.rs`: (i) the test-grade KEM keypair derivation rule is centralized in `derive_test_kem_keypair_from_validator_id(vid)` and is the single source of truth for both the listener (`ServerHandshakeConfig.local_kem_sk` / delegation cert `leaf_kem_pk`) and the dialer (`ClientConnectionConfig.peer_kem_pk`), so two real `qbind-node` processes can actually complete the KEMTLS handshake instead of failing with `Net(Protocol("client handle_server_accept failed"))`; (ii) the local NodeId, `SimpleValidatorNodeMapping` NodeId, and the dialer's outbound NodeId are now all derived via the same `sha3_256_tagged("QBIND:nodeid:v1", test_kem_pk(vid))` rule (`derive_test_node_id_from_validator_id`), so `send_to(ValidatorId)` resolves to the *same* NodeId the transport actually registered for that connection; (iii) `--p2p-peer` now accepts `vid@addr` syntax (parsed by `parse_peer_spec`), and per-peer `peer_kem_pk` + `validator_id` overrides are threaded into `TcpKemTlsP2pService::dial_peer` via `set_peer_kem_pk_overrides` / `set_peer_validator_id_overrides` so each side dials with the *peer's* test-grade KEM public key and the *peer's* expected validator id (the latter satisfies the protocol-level `delegation_cert.validator_id == client_init.validator_id` check in `qbind_net::handshake::handle_server_accept`). A latent inbound-side bug was also fixed: `TcpStream::into_std()` keeps the socket non-blocking, but `accept_kemtls_async` does blocking reads, so the inbound handshake was tripping `WouldBlock` on the very first read — `handle_inbound_connection` now restores blocking mode before the handshake. Multi-validator binary-path runs that pass bare-addr peers (no `vid@`) are rejected with a clear `B7: --p2p-peer entries must be of the form 'vid@addr'…` error rather than silently producing a broken handshake. A `PeerValidatorMap` is populated at dial-config time (`P2pNodeContext.peer_validator_map`) so the connected peer is recognized as `ValidatorId(N)` on the dialer side. Regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b7_kemtls_bringup_identity_closure_tests.rs` (5 integration tests including a bounded two-real-binary KEMTLS handshake proof — the exact case Run 005 failed to demonstrate) and by 6 new unit tests under `p2p_node_builder::tests::b7_*`. The fix is bounded to the test-grade DevNet path and does not invent any new identity / certificate system. • ✅ **B8** — listener-side test-grade validator-identity closure + bounded initial-dial retry: the smallest honest fix to the negative finding of DevNet Evidence Run 006 (the two `Run 006` narrowing items in the previous `Inbound-side validator identity binding (B7-residual)` bullet). Three concrete changes: **(i) Listener-side identity closure.** A new `accept_kemtls_async_with_peer_init` variant in `crates/qbind-node/src/secure_channel.rs` surfaces the dialer-supplied `ClientInit.client_random` and `ClientInit.validator_id` (via `qbind_net::unpack_client_init`) from the server-side accept path. `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_tcp.rs` now exposes `set_inbound_identity_resolver` / `InboundIdentityResolver`, and `handle_inbound_connection` consults the installed resolver: if it returns `Some(deterministic_node_id)` the accepted session is registered under that NodeId, otherwise the legacy temporary-session-NodeId path is preserved exactly (no silent override). `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs` installs a resolver that recovers the dialer's vid from the deterministic `qbind-client-<N>` ASCII prefix `create_connection_configs` already places in `client_random` (parsed by the new `parse_test_validator_id_from_client_random` helper) and returns `derive_test_node_id_from_validator_id(N)` — the SAME NodeId the dialer side registers under. **(ii) Bounded initial-dial retry.** A new `DialRetryPolicy` (default 8 attempts × {100..1000}ms ≈ 5.5 s) and `set_dial_retry_policy` on `TcpKemTlsP2pService`. `start()` no longer blocks on dial; instead it spawns a per-peer background `DialerHandle::dial_with_retry` task that retries only transient TCP errors (`ConnectionRefused`, `ConnectionReset`, `ConnectionAborted`, `TimedOut`, `AddrNotAvailable`, `NotFound`) and bounds attempts + backoff. KEMTLS-handshake errors and configuration errors are NOT retried. `shutdown()` aborts in-flight dial tasks before shutting peer connections. Single-validator / no-static-peers / LocalMesh paths are bit-equivalent (no dial tasks spawned at all). **(iii) Honest scope.** Resolver semantics under the current `MutualAuthMode::Disabled` test-grade path are explicitly documented as self-asserted: a malicious dialer could spoof a vid in `client_random`. Strictly cryptographic peer-identity binding still requires `MutualAuthMode::Required` and is kept as a separate `Remaining` bullet below. The B8 fix is bounded to the test-grade DevNet binary path and does not invent any new identity / certificate system. Files touched: `crates/qbind-node/src/secure_channel.rs`, `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_tcp.rs`, `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs`. Regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b8_listener_identity_closure_and_dial_retry_tests.rs` (6 tests: parse round-trip, listener-side deterministic-NodeId binding, initial-dial retry recovery from stagger, two-node bidirectional `connected_peers` precondition, single-validator no-regression, `DialRetryPolicy::no_retry` pin). All B7 tests, all 5 c4_b6 tests, all 16 three_node_kemtls_integration tests, all 9 t172 P2P smoke tests, all 10 t175 wiring tests, and all 604 lib unit tests continue to pass. • ✅ **B9** — leader-side re-emission of `BroadcastProposal` on late peer connect within the same view (the smallest honest fix to the negative finding of DevNet Evidence Run 007). The fix is bounded entirely to the binary-path consensus loop (no engine redesign, no transport redesign): `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` gains an optional `peer_connectivity: Option<Arc<dyn PeerConnectivitySource>>` (a tiny dedicated trait — strictly smaller than `P2pService` — implemented by the new `P2pServicePeerConnectivity` adapter that forwards to the same `Arc<dyn P2pService>` already backing inbound demuxing and outbound `P2pConsensusNetwork`, so connectivity, outbound, and inbound observations all come from the same transport instance). `do_leader_tick` now caches the leader's last `BroadcastProposal` together with the view it was emitted for; on every tick the new `maybe_reemit_on_late_peer_connect` helper runs through seven explicit boundedness gates: (1) **transition required** — at least one NodeId in the current connected set was absent from the previous tick's set; (2) **cached proposal required** — the engine actually emitted a leader-step proposal at some point; (3) **view match** — `engine.current_view() == cached_view` (a view advance drops the cache without re-broadcast); (4) **leader of current view** — `engine.is_leader_for_current_view()` holds; (5) **commit not invalidated** — `committed_height` has not reached or passed the cached view; (6) **per-view single-shot** — a `reemitted_for_view: Option<u64>` latch that fires at most once per view regardless of how many peers connect or how many ticks pass; (7) **outbound facade required** — the loop must actually have somewhere to broadcast. On all-gates-pass the loop calls `outbound.broadcast_proposal(&cached)` exactly once and increments a new `BinaryConsensusLoopInboundStats::outbound_proposal_late_peer_reemits` counter (also surfaced in the `Loop exit:` summary line). Reconnect churn within the same view produces zero additional re-emits (gate 6); a view change between cache-fill and the connectivity poll invalidates the cache and produces zero stale replays (gate 3); when `peer_connectivity = None` (single-validator P2P, LocalMesh, the `io=None` 4-arg loop) the entire B9 path is skipped and the counter stays at 0 — bit-equivalent to the pre-B9 loop. Files touched: `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` (new trait + new adapter + cache state + reemit helper + counter + `BinaryConsensusLoopIo::peer_connectivity` field), `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` (`run_p2p_node` wires the same `Arc<dyn P2pService>` instance through `P2pServicePeerConnectivity`). Regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b9_late_peer_connect_proposal_reemit_tests.rs` (6 tests: A — late peer connect triggers exactly one bounded re-emission; B — per-view single-shot latch holds across reconnect churn (exactly 1 re-emit when view 0 stays current); C — view-change invalidation drops stale cache (0 stale replays across multiple view advances); D — peer connected before first proposal stays bounded (≤ 1 across 40 ticks); E — `peer_connectivity = None` regression guard (counter stays 0); F — `io = None` LocalMesh regression guard). All pre-existing tests continue to pass: 604 lib unit tests, 5 c4_b6 tests, 6 b8 tests, 5 b7 tests, 6 b5 tests, 4 b1/b2/b4 tests, 13 LocalMesh tests, 3 b3 tests. The B9 fix does NOT redesign consensus, does NOT redesign transport, does NOT replace B6/B7/B8, does NOT introduce harness-only logic on the binary path, and does NOT broaden into mutual-auth PKI or production identity hardening (those remain in the open `Remaining` bullets below). • ⚠️ Multi-validator restore semantics (P2P chain catchup above the snapshot prefix) — out of scope for B5/B6/B7/B8/B9. • ✅ **B12 — mutual-auth (`MutualAuthMode::Required`) cryptographic peer-identity binding on the binary path.** The smallest honest closure of the C4 residual previously labelled "Mutual-auth (`MutualAuthMode::Required`) cryptographic peer-identity binding (B8-residual)". The `qbind-net` mutual-auth handshake codepath (`ServerHandshake::handle_client_init` parsing + verifying a v2 `ClientInit.client_cert`, transcript-binding the cert into the AEAD key schedule, and producing `HandshakeResult { peer_validator_id, client_node_id, mutual_auth_complete }`) **already existed** before B12 — the identity-binding gap was strictly that the `qbind-node` binary stack discarded those fields at the `Connection` boundary and the listener-side resolver consumed only the dialer's self-asserted `ClientInit.client_random`. B12 wires that already-existing path end-to-end through the binary-path P2P stack with five bounded changes: (i) `qbind-net::Connection` retains `peer_validator_id` / `peer_node_id` / `mutual_auth_complete` after handshake completion (previously dropped) and exposes them via `peer_validator_id()` / `peer_node_id()` / `mutual_auth_complete()` accessors — captured at the *exact* `Established` transition site for both server (`handle_client_init`) and client (`handle_server_accept`) paths so values are populated for any caller that holds an established `Connection`; (ii) `qbind-node::secure_channel::AcceptedPeerInit` gains `verified_peer_validator_id: Option<[u8; 32]>` / `verified_client_node_id: Option<[u8; 32]>` / `mutual_auth_complete: bool`, populated in `SecureChannel::from_accepted_with_peer_init` from the `Connection` accessors, and these fields are surfaced to the inbound resolver alongside the legacy self-asserted `client_random` / `validator_id`; (iii) `qbind-node::p2p_node_builder::P2pNodeBuilder` gains a `with_mutual_auth_mode(MutualAuthMode)` builder that defaults to `Disabled` (preserves pre-B12 behaviour bit-for-bit), and `create_connection_configs` honors it by attaching the local `NetworkDelegationCert` as `local_client_cert` (so the dialer presents a v2 `ClientInit`), setting `ServerHandshakeConfig.mutual_auth_mode = Required`, and installing a `TrustedClientRoots` resolver so the listener actually exercises `parse_and_verify_client_cert`; (iv) the listener-side `InboundIdentityResolver` is split by mode — under `Required`/`Optional` it sources identity ONLY from the verified cert (`AcceptedPeerInit.verified_peer_validator_id` parsed via the new `parse_test_validator_id_from_cert_validator_id` and mapped through `derive_test_node_id_from_validator_id` to the SAME deterministic NodeId both ends register under), and **fails closed** (returns `None`) when `mutual_auth_complete = false` so the self-asserted `client_random` path is unreachable; under `Disabled` the pre-B12 B8 self-asserted resolver is preserved exactly; (v) `qbind-node::main::run_p2p_node` plumbs `--p2p-mutual-auth required|optional|disabled` (and the `QBIND_MUTUAL_AUTH` env var as a fallback) through `with_mutual_auth_mode`, with an explicit `[binary] B12: mutual_auth_mode=… (source: …)` startup banner so evidence runs can prove which mode was active. **Identity property cryptographically bound that was not before:** under `Required` mode the listener-side accepted-session NodeId is derived from `cert.validator_id`, where `cert` is the dialer's `NetworkDelegationCert` whose `leaf_kem_pk` participates in the AEAD transcript hash AND whose `sig_bytes` is verified against the configured `TrustedClientRoots` root — so completing the handshake AND producing a routable session-bound NodeId requires (a) holding the leaf KEM secret matching `cert.leaf_kem_pk` (the protocol-level KEMTLS commitment) and (b) producing a cert whose signature passes the configured signature suite. Under `Disabled` mode (the pre-B12 default and DevNet convenience path) the resolver's input is still the self-asserted `client_random` and is documented as such; B12 explicitly does **not** silently relabel test-grade behaviour as hardened — the two modes are byte-for-byte distinguishable on the wire (v1 vs v2 `ClientInit`) and at the resolver call site (different `match` arm). **Migration / compatibility:** `Disabled` (the pre-B12 default) is preserved bit-for-bit. Files touched: `crates/qbind-net/src/connection.rs` (peer-identity capture + accessors), `crates/qbind-node/src/secure_channel.rs` (`AcceptedPeerInit` extension + populate from `Connection`), `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs` (`with_mutual_auth_mode` + cert + roots + cert-verified resolver + `parse_test_validator_id_from_cert_validator_id`), `crates/qbind-node/src/cli.rs` (`--p2p-mutual-auth`), `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` (env+CLI plumbing through builder, banner). Regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b12_mutual_auth_identity_binding_tests.rs` (6 tests: A — two-node `Required`-mode handshake succeeds and BOTH sides see each other's deterministic NodeId sourced from the verified cert; B — `Required`-mode resolver refuses self-asserted identity when `mutual_auth_complete = false` (the closed-form contract pin: a cert whose `validator_id` field carries the dialer's `qbind-client-N` shape returns `None` from `parse_test_validator_id_from_cert_validator_id`, so the self-asserted shape cannot spoof a routable vid even under cert-shaped delivery); C — bidirectional `broadcast(Heartbeat)` under `Required` mode resolves to the cert-bound session on the listener; D — `Disabled` mode preserves B7 dialer-side closure AND B8 listener-side self-asserted closure bit-for-bit; E — `parse_test_validator_id_from_cert_validator_id` round-trips for valid `qbind-val-N` shapes and rejects all non-conforming bytes (all-zero, `qbind-client-N` shape, `qbind-val-not-a-number`); F — single-validator `Required`-mode build/shutdown is clean). All pre-B12 regression suites continue to pass: 604 lib unit tests, 5 b7, 6 b8, 6 b9, 10 b10, 5 b11, 5 c4_b6, 4 b1/b2/b4, 6 b5, 3 b3, 9 t172, 25 t175 wiring, 10 t175 config, 17 m8 mutual-auth config, 16 three_node_kemtls, plus 13 qbind-net integration suites (m8 mutual-auth net-level included). The B12 fix does NOT redesign consensus, does NOT redesign transport, does NOT invent a parallel identity framework (it strictly wires the existing `qbind-net::handshake` mutual-auth path), and does NOT change the test-grade DummySig signature surface — production-grade PQC root-key distribution and cert lifecycle remain outside scope and are tracked under the remaining bullet below. **What B12 does NOT close:** (a) the `TrustedClientRoots` resolver currently returns a deterministic 32-byte dummy root key for any `root_key_id`, and the test-grade DummySig provider accepts certs whose `sig_bytes` starts with `0x00` — so the cert *signature path* is exercised structurally (a dialer with a non-test-grade or tampered sig would be rejected by the chosen suite) but is not yet exercising real PQC verification against a real long-term validator root key; production root-key distribution (and the operational PKI behind it) is still tracked separately as a `Remaining` bullet below. (b) The deterministic test-grade `qbind-val-<N>` validator-id ↔ KEM-pk mapping is the same one B7/B8 use; replacing it with a production-grade per-validator cert lifecycle is intentionally not part of B12. **Justification for first mutual-auth binary-path evidence run:** yes — this is enough. Under `--p2p-mutual-auth required`, the binary now (1) presents a client cert on every dial, (2) parses + verifies it on the listener via the existing `parse_and_verify_client_cert`, (3) transcript-binds it into the AEAD key schedule, (4) registers the accepted session under a NodeId derived from the cert's `validator_id` (no longer from `client_random`), and (5) routes consensus traffic through the same B6/B7/B8/B9/B10/B11 pipeline that already produces sustained QC formation in Run 009. • ⚠️ Validator/node-id identity hardening for production (today's `SimpleValidatorNodeMapping` is intentionally simple, suitable for the first binary-path evidence run but not production). • ⚠️ Real PQC KEMTLS handshake / identity certificate path on the binary (test-grade transport now actually completes; production identity binding still tracked separately). • ⚠️ Inbound timeout / new-view (`ConsensusNetMsg::Timeout`, `ConsensusNetMsg::NewView`) routing into the engine on the binary path — counted as "received but unhandled" today, intentionally deferred. • ⚠️ Extend restore beyond VM-v0 substate if/when other substores grow snapshot semantics — not currently produced by `StateSnapshotter`. • ⚠️ **Engine-side acceptance / QC-formation closure on the binary path under post-B9 re-emitted leader proposal (B9-residual).** Surfaced empirically by DevNet Evidence Run 008 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_008.md`): two real `qbind-node` binaries now move a cross-node `ConsensusNetMsg::Proposal` and a return `ConsensusNetMsg::Vote` between each other for the first time (B9 re-emit fires exactly once per view as designed; loop-exit counters `outbound_proposals=1`, `inbound_proposals=1` on the peer, `outbound_votes=1` on the peer, `inbound_votes=1` on the leader), but `qbind_consensus_proposals_total{result="accepted"} = 0` on the receiver and `qbind_consensus_votes_total{result="accepted"} = 0` on the leader, so `qcs_formed_total = 0` and `committed_height = None` on both nodes across three scrapes. The reason — view / proposer-index mismatch on the re-emitted cached proposal versus the receiver's local view, an accept-path metric-increment gap, or a test-grade signature/cert field that the engine validates but the post-B7/B8 Disabled-mutual-auth configuration leaves at a non-canonical value — is not yet identified. B10 is the smallest honest closure of this residual on the binary path; it is intentionally below B6/B7/B8/B9 in scope and does not redesign consensus, transport, or identity. **Empirically closed on real binaries by DevNet Evidence Run 009 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_009.md`):** post-B10 sustained QC formation on both V0 and V1 across three monotonic `/metrics` scrapes (`qbind_consensus_qcs_formed_total` 358 → 1 062 on V0, 359 → 1 063 on V1) and `committed_height > None` on both nodes (V0 `Some(1 453)`, V1 `Some(1 452)` at shutdown). This bullet is therefore retained for traceability but its empirical residual on real binaries is closed. • ✅ **B11** — `consensus_net_*_total` Prometheus counter coverage on the `P2pConsensusNetwork` path. Surfaced for the first time by Run 008 (now that messages actually cross the wire): the loop-level `outbound_proposals` / `inbound_proposals` / `outbound_votes` / `inbound_votes` counters in the binary's `Loop exit:` summary honestly record `1` of each, while `consensus_net_outbound_total{kind="proposal_broadcast"}` / `…{kind="vote_broadcast"}` / `consensus_net_inbound_total{kind="proposal"}` / `…{kind="vote"}` stayed at `0` across all three `/metrics` scrapes in Run 008 and remained at `0` in the otherwise-fully-positive Run 009 ("the only respect in which Run 009 is not 'complete-positive across every metric surface'"). The Prometheus family under-reported (did not fabricate) the `P2pConsensusNetwork` path actually used by the binary; the `inc_outbound_proposal_broadcast` / `inc_inbound_proposal` increments lived on the `consensus_net_worker.rs` codepath and were not reached under the binary's actual configuration. **Closed by B11 (this delta).** Two minimal, additive changes to the real binary path: (i) `crates/qbind-node/src/consensus_net_p2p.rs` — `P2pConsensusNetwork` gains an optional `Arc<NodeMetrics>` (wired by the new `with_metrics(...)` builder method) and increments `consensus_net_outbound_total{kind="proposal_broadcast"}` / `…{kind="vote_broadcast"}` / `…{kind="vote_send_to"}` exactly once per successful `broadcast_proposal` / `broadcast_vote` / `send_vote_to` call (counted *after* the underlying `P2pService` call returns, so the counter reflects what was actually pushed to the transport — not what was merely attempted; `send_vote_to` for an unknown validator returns an error and does not increment, by direct test). When `with_metrics(...)` is not called, the facade is bit-equivalent to its pre-B11 behaviour (no counter increments at all). (ii) `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs::handle_inbound_consensus_msg` — every inbound `ConsensusNetMsg` is counted exactly once before any decode/accept gating: `Proposal(...)` → `inbound_total{kind="proposal"}`, `Vote(...)` → `inbound_total{kind="vote"}`, `Timeout(...)` / `NewView(...)` → `inbound_total{kind="other"}` (so the existing "received but unhandled" frames are not silently absorbed). Counts mirror the same frames the loop-level `inbound_msgs_received` / `inbound_proposals_delivered` / `inbound_votes_delivered` counters already observe — no fabricated increments, no double counting. (iii) `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs::run_p2p_node` wires the production `Arc<NodeMetrics>` into the outbound `P2pConsensusNetwork` via `.with_metrics(Arc::clone(&node_metrics))`. The `forward_actions_to_facade` boundary inside the loop deliberately does **not** count outbound — counting there in addition to the facade would double-count; the engine ↔ facade boundary stays metric-free and the facade is the single increment site for outbound. Files touched: `crates/qbind-node/src/consensus_net_p2p.rs` (+`metrics: Option<Arc<NodeMetrics>>`, `with_metrics(...)`, three `inc_outbound_*` call sites), `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` (one match in `handle_inbound_consensus_msg` covering `Proposal` / `Vote` / `Timeout` / `NewView`), `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` (one `.with_metrics(...)` call). Regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b11_consensus_net_prometheus_coverage_tests.rs` (5 high-signal tests: A — pre-fix shape preserved when `with_metrics(...)` is not called (counters stay at 0, no hidden mutation), B — every facade call increments exactly the matching outbound counter exactly once and an erroring `send_vote_to(unknown)` does not increment, C — every inbound `ConsensusNetMsg` increments exactly the matching inbound counter (4 proposals → 4, 3 votes → 3, 2 timeouts → 2 under `kind="other"`), D — B9 single-shot late-peer-connect re-emit moves the outbound counter by exactly +1 with no double-counting, E — `io = None` / single-validator LocalMesh path leaves the entire `consensus_net_*_total` family at 0 (B1/B2 bit-equivalence)). All pre-existing B-series tests continue to pass: 604 lib unit tests, 5 c4_b6 tests, 6 b9 tests, 10 b10 tests, 6 b8 tests, 5 b7 tests, 6 b5 tests, 4 b1/b2/b4 tests, 13 LocalMesh tests, 3 b3 tests. The B11 fix does NOT redesign networking, does NOT redesign consensus, does NOT touch B9/B10 logic, does NOT broaden into production identity hardening, and does NOT silently fix the contradiction-file header `Version`/`Date` mismatch (kept as a separate documentation-hygiene item). What remains in C4 is now strictly (a) production identity hardening (mutual-auth `MutualAuthMode::Required`, real PQC certs) and (b) multi-validator restore catchup (P2P chain catchup above the snapshot prefix). |
| **Tracking** | Recorded by `docs/protocol/QBIND_REPO_CODE_DOC_ALIGNMENT_AUDIT.md` §6.1–§6.3, §9 (B1, B2, B3) as the top three execution blockers exposed by EXE-1. B1 + B2 closed by `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs` + `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` (regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/binary_path_b1_b2_b4_tests.rs`). B3 closed by `crates/qbind-node/src/snapshot_restore.rs` + `--restore-from-snapshot` CLI flag in `crates/qbind-node/src/cli.rs` + restore call in `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs` (regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b3_snapshot_restore_tests.rs`). B5 closed by `BasicHotStuffEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline` + `HotStuffStateEngine::initialize_from_snapshot_baseline` in `crates/qbind-consensus/` and `RestoreBaseline` / `BinaryConsensusLoopConfig::with_restore_baseline` in `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs`, with the `RestoreOutcome → RestoreBaseline` translation in `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs`; regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b5_restore_aware_consensus_start_tests.rs`. **B6** closed by the inbound-subscribe fix in `crates/qbind-node/src/p2p_node_builder.rs`, the new `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` / `run_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` / `spawn_binary_consensus_loop_with_io` surface in `crates/qbind-node/src/binary_consensus_loop.rs`, and the `run_p2p_node` wiring in `crates/qbind-node/src/main.rs`; regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/c4_b6_p2p_binary_path_interconnect_tests.rs` (inbound proposal → engine vote, two-engine cross-wired progression past view 0, single-validator io=None unchanged, inbound-close survival, non-leader proposal not silently dropped). First end-to-end binary-path multi-validator exercise recorded by `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_005.md`: B6 wiring observable in the running binary (multi-validator banner emitted; `BinaryConsensusLoopIo` active; `inbound_msgs` / `inbound_proposals` / `inbound_votes` counters surfaced in `Loop exit` summary on both nodes), but no `ConsensusNetMsg` crossed between two real `qbind-node` processes due to the binary-path test-grade KEMTLS bring-up gap recorded in the new `Remaining` bullet above. Second end-to-end binary-path multi-validator exercise (post-B7) recorded by `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_006.md`: KEMTLS handshake now succeeds between two real `qbind-node` processes and dialer-side peer-validator identity closure is observable on the binary, but `inbound_msgs = 0` on both nodes still — listener-side temporary-NodeId binding combined with a single-direction-only TCP topology (initial-dial `Connection refused` not retried) prevents V0's `BroadcastProposal` from resolving to a registered transport session for V1; the §11 single-validator LocalMesh regression check on the same binary observed `commits = 200`, `committed_height = Some(199)`, no regression. **Third end-to-end binary-path multi-validator exercise (post-B8) recorded by `docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_007.md`: B8 listener-side identity resolver line and B8 bounded-retry trace are both observable on the binary; both sides register each other's deterministic NodeId for the first time in DevNet evidence (`Peer NodeId(92115fddcd4f93a0) connected` on V0 after the resolver bound the inbound, and `Peer NodeId(4bd96f97b1aaec9d) connected` on V1); however `consensus_net_outbound_total{kind="proposal_broadcast"} = 0` on V0 and `inbound_proposals=0`, `qbind_consensus_proposals_total{result="accepted"} = 0` on V1 across three `/metrics` scrapes — V0's leader emitted view 0's `BroadcastProposal` before V1 connected and the engine did not re-emit on late peer connect; §11 single-validator LocalMesh regression check observed `commits = 345`, `committed_height = Some(344)`, `view = 347`, no regression. The Run-007 boundary is strictly below the Run-006 listener-identity boundary that B8 closed; this engine-broadcast boundary is in turn closed by B9 (above), making Run 008 — first observed cross-node proposal/vote/QC/commit progression on real `qbind-node` processes — reachable on the binary path. B9 closure regression-tested by `crates/qbind-node/tests/b9_late_peer_connect_proposal_reemit_tests.rs` (6 tests covering A — exactly-one re-emit on late connect, B — per-view single-shot under reconnect churn, C — view-change invalidation, D — pre-connected peer bounded, E — `peer_connectivity=None` regression guard, F — `io=None` LocalMesh regression guard).** |

**Run 024 C4 snapshot-trigger note (2026-05-09):** DevNet Evidence Run 024 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_024.md`) negatively proved the real binary's periodic `--snapshot-interval-blocks` trigger is not wired end-to-end.
V0 ran N=4 Required-mode with `--snapshot-dir`, `--snapshot-interval-blocks 4`, and `--snapshot-max-snapshots 2`, advanced to `committed_height=54` without SIGUSR1, and stayed alive, but `/tmp/run024/snapshots/` remained empty and `qbind_snapshot_success_total` / `qbind_snapshot_last_height` stayed zero.
This does not regress the Run 022/023 SIGUSR1-created real snapshot path, but it leaves periodic height-triggered real-binary snapshots open under C4.


#### C4 Run 021 evidence update (2026-05-09)

DevNet Evidence Run 021 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_021.md`) materially reopens the latest claimed VM-v0 runtime-open / SIGUSR1 snapshot-trigger closure on real binaries. The tested `qbind-node` at commit `950ce2b5e925b2162b1df3da840fa0b35e05dd36` (sha256 `69223f70ff05ebc0030633c84d0a2c77e8d4052cee2325a7a62262f13c18199f`, BuildID `97fd927c08c5a3eb64ac01f93e20b318f00f30ea`) rejected `--snapshot-dir` as an unexpected argument, exposed no `--snapshot-max-snapshots` help surface, did not create/open `<data_dir>/state_vm_v0` during a secondary vm-v0 live run, and terminated on SIGUSR1 (`wait_status=-10`) rather than logging signal receipt or invoking `StateSnapshotter::create_snapshot`. No SIGUSR1-created snapshot existed, so B3/B5/B13/B14 preservation from that snapshot remains unproven. C4 therefore remains open for real-binary VM-v0 runtime-open and in-process snapshot-trigger operability.

#### C4 Run 022 evidence update (2026-05-09)

DevNet Evidence Run 022 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_022.md`) positively closes the specific Run 021 regression on the tested real binary: `qbind-node --help` exposes `--snapshot-dir`, `--snapshot-interval-blocks`, and `--snapshot-max-snapshots`; `--execution-profile vm-v0 --data-dir <dir>` opens `<data_dir>/state_vm_v0` at startup; SIGUSR1 is handled without process termination; configured SIGUSR1 invokes `StateSnapshotter::create_snapshot` in-process on the opened VM-v0 RocksDB handle; and B3/B5 restore from that SIGUSR1-created snapshot succeeds. C4 remains open overall for the broader production items already listed (including production fast-sync/consensus-storage restore and production PQC root-key distribution), and Run 022 did not repeat the full N=4 Required-mode B13/B14 continuation shape.

#### C4 Run 085 evidence update (2026-05-18)

DevNet Evidence Run 085 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_085.md`) narrows C4 further with committed N=4 MainNet release-binary peer-candidate `0x05` validation-only evidence. The harness `scripts/devnet/run_085_mainnet_peer_candidate_0x05_matrix.sh` mints signed MainNet trust material, launches four release `qbind-node` processes with explicit trust-bundle signing key, per-node data dirs, peer leaf mappings, and no `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback, then passes baseline startup, valid send/validate, receiver-disabled cheap-ignore, invalid/wrong-chain reject, and duplicate-suppression scenarios. The evidence preserves the Run 084 non-mutation guarantees: no peer-driven live apply, no propagation/rebroadcast, no sequence mutation, no `LivePqcTrustState` mutation, no session eviction, no active DummySig/DummyKem/DummyAead, and no fallback root. C4 remains open for peer-driven live apply / propagation, `activation_epoch` runtime sourcing, KMS/HSM custody, in-binary/on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation, and broader production KEMTLS lifecycle/readiness boundaries. C5 is not closed by this run.

#### C4 Run 086 evidence update (2026-05-18)

DevNet Evidence Run 086 (`docs/devnet/QBIND_DEVNET_EVIDENCE_RUN_086.md`) is a **documentation-only** update of the operator lifecycle runbook (`docs/ops/QBIND_PQC_TRUST_LIFECYCLE_RUNBOOK.md`) covering the peer-candidate `0x05` validation-only lifecycle landed by Runs 076–085. The runbook gains a new §6.G that documents (i) strict behaviour — validation-only; observe valid; reject invalid; suppress duplicates; cheap-ignore receiver-disabled; never apply; never write the sequence file; never mutate `LivePqcTrustState`; never evict sessions; never propagate/rebroadcast; (ii) feature evolution Run 076 → Run 085; (iii) allowed operator use (observe / validate / produce evidence / decide manually whether to use §6.F.4 SIGHUP live reload-apply); (iv) forbidden operator interpretations (not propagation; not peer-driven live apply; not consensus ratification; not automatic root rotation; not automatic revocation distribution); (v) per-scenario safety invariants (sequence-hash invariance, live-reload-apply metrics = 0, session-eviction metrics = 0, NOT applied / not propagated log lines, no `--p2p-trusted-root` fallback, no active DummySig/DummyKem/DummyAead, cert-verify rejected = 0 for honest traffic, peer-candidate rejected counters move only for invalid candidates); (vi) Run 085 as the strongest current MainNet evidence summary; and (vii) explicit non-closure list (peer-driven live apply / propagation, `activation_epoch` runtime source, KMS/HSM, signing-key ratification, fast-sync restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation remain OPEN). §10 residual risks is updated to record that Runs 076–085 added an observation-only `0x05` exchange while explicitly preserving "peer-driven live apply / propagation remains OPEN". §11 mapping table is extended with Runs 076–086. §12 glossary is extended with the six hidden peer-candidate CLI flags from Runs 077 / 079 / 080. No `crates/**/src/**` source was changed by Run 086 (no contradiction was found between the runbook prose and the observed implementation in `pqc_trust_peer_candidate.rs`, `pqc_peer_candidate_binary.rs`, `pqc_peer_candidate_wire.rs`, `p2p_tcp.rs`, `p2p_node_builder.rs`, `main.rs`, `cli.rs`, and `metrics.rs`). Run 086 narrows operator-documentation coverage; it does **not** narrow C4 or C5 closure. C4 and C5 remain OPEN as listed in the Run 085 update above; peer-driven live apply / propagation, `activation_epoch` runtime sourcing, KMS/HSM custody, in-binary/on-chain signing-key ratification, production fast-sync / consensus-storage restore, per-environment production trust-anchor operation, and broader production KEMTLS lifecycle/readiness boundaries remain open. `cargo check -p qbind-node --bin qbind-node` passes.

### C3. Reporter Rewards Not Implemented

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| **Status** | ⚠️ **OPEN** |
| **Whitepaper Reference** | Section 12.2 (Slashing Model), Section 12.2.3 (Reporter Incentives) |
| **Code Location** | `crates/qbind-types/src/state_governance.rs:52` (`reporter_reward_bps` field) |
| **Description** | `reporter_reward_bps` parameter exists in `ParamRegistry` but no code distributes rewards. Evidence reporting has no incentive mechanism. Whitepaper Section 12.2.3 now explicitly documents this as future work. |
| **Impact** | Low-Medium - No monetary incentive; however reporting is hardened and abuse-resistant (M15). |
| **M15 Mitigation** | Evidence ingestion hardened with 8-step verification ordering: (1) Reporter validation, (2) Size bounds, (3) Per-block cap, (4) Deduplication, (5) Structure validation, (6) Age bounds, (7) Future height check, (8) Cryptographic verification (expensive - last). Config: `require_validator_reporter=true`, `per_block_evidence_cap=10`, `max_evidence_age_blocks=100K`, size limits per offense type. See `crates/qbind-consensus/src/slashing/mod.rs` (`HardenedEvidenceIngestionEngine`). |
| **M20 Documentation** | Whitepaper Section 12.2.3 "Reporter Incentives (Future Work)" added. Explicitly states: no on-chain reporter rewards currently; slashing is purely punitive; any future reward model must build on M15 hardened evidence pipeline. |
| **Remaining** | • Wire `reporter_reward_bps` to slashing engine reward distribution • Add reward transfer in penalty application path • Design and implement tokenomics for reporter incentives |
